Conflicting Cultures: Linking Agency, Community, and University in a Community Building Endeavor

Author: Matsuoka, Jon K1; Mulroy, Elizabeth A; Umemoto, Karen1 School Social Work, U Hawaii, Honolulu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61538338?accountid=14667

Abstract: This paper is based on a case study that reflects a collaborative effort between a university & a nongovernmental organization that serves the native Hawaiian community. The organization, which was undergoing a paradigm shift, sought support from university faculty. The shift in orientation was played out at the community level as a team of professionals worked with community leaders to create a vision & a community development strategy based on resident input. The novel qualities of this collaborative contributed to numerous lessons learned on all sides & will be used in future endeavors involving multiple partners. 15 References. Two Concepts of Charity and Their Relationship to Social Work Practice

Author: Friedman, Bruce D11 Coll Osteopathic Medicine, Michigan State U, Lansing friedm52@msu.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61534790?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Judeo Christian concept of charity is inherent in the US social welfare system. Two differing views of charity, one Jewish & the other Christian, must be defined & weighed if their respective contributions are to be properly understood. The dichotomy between these two concepts is explored & related to the development of social welfare institutions in the US. The result is then related to the field of social work & the role that these concepts play in empowering clients. 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

Paternalism in Supervisory Relationships

Author: Greene, Kenneth R11 School Social Work, U Georgia, Athens kengreene@writeme.com

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61486493?accountid=14667

Abstract: Supervision is a vital part of practice for many social workers. In many settings, social workers must provide administrative as well as clinical supervision. Social work supervision is filled with ethical dilemmas due to the unequal power relationship between supervisor & supervises. Charles Levy (1973) proposes five principles to prevent the misuse of supervisory power. These principles may create another dilemma that stems not from a selfish disregard for the supervisees, but from a sincere desire to do what is best. This article will describe & analyze paternalism as it relates to supervision using two case examples & W. D. Ross's (1960) theory of ethics. 1 Figure, 16 References. Blending Service and Financial Security: A Study in the Organizational Adaptation of a Fraternal Benefit Society

Author: Solt, Barbara E11 Instit Advancement Social Work Research

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61536341?accountid=14667

Abstract: A little known organizational model rooted in earliest social welfare history, the fraternal benefit society, is presented as a case study in organizational adaptation to changing internal & environmental pressures. The fraternal benefit society combines elements associated with commerce, human services, & self help groups. Rooted in early Greek & Roman mutual aid societies, the fraternal benefit movement paralleled the development of social services since the mid 19th century, & in many ways serves as a prototype for newly emerging organizations that seek to combine elements of economic development with social welfare service provision. Fraternals present structural issues also seen in organizations in which employee shareholders benefit from the commercial success of the company in which they work. The writer uses Lawrence & Lorsch's Contingency Theory to analyze how one fraternal has adapted to become a major financial & voluntary service institution. Gordon & Babchuk's Typology of Instrumental & Affinitive Organizations is used to discuss the dynamic tension inherent within the fraternal structure. 1 Table, 18 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Jewish Community Center and Its Social Work Guests: A Review of the Literature

Author: Sweifach, Jay11 Wurzweiler School Social Work, Yeshiva U, New York, NY

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61486532?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Jewish Community Center (JCC) movement & social work share a common history & many common values. Jewish agencies were founded, staffed, & maintained by social workers. Over time, a variety of phenomena have influenced & changed the nature of practice within the center field. This paper will review both empirical & theoretical literature related to the interactions & interrelationships between JCCs & social work, focusing on what is known about social work as a "guest" discipline in the JCC. In order to provide context & clarity, a review of literature related to the status of social work in other types of host agencies (eg, hospitals & schools) is also included. 106 References. Conceptualizing Spirituality in Social Work: How the Metaphysical Beliefs of Social Workers May Foster Bias toward Theistic Consumers

Author: Hodge, David11 George Warren Brown School Social Work, Washington U, Saint Louis, MO

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61512494?accountid=14667

Abstract: In spite of the growing interest in spirituality, little attention has been paid to how social workers' metaphysical worldviews affect their conceptualization & subsequent operationalization of spirituality. This paper explores how the largely nontheistic worldviews of social workers inform their definitions of spirituality, which in turn fosters a systemic bias against the spirituality of consumers who hold theistic belief systems. Examples of how current definitions conflict with a theistic worldview are provided, & it is suggested that the operationalization of existing conceptualizations would yield biased measures that would preassign theistic consumers a lower level of spirituality. Suggestions for addressing the problem conclude the paper. 4 Tables, 1 Figure, 78 References. Adapted from the source document.

C.S. Loch and M. Richmond's Genesis of the Social Situation and Social Work

Author: Majonis, Joel11 Renison Coll, U Waterloo, Ontario

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61485851?accountid=14667

Abstract: C. S Loch developed an "organized charity" containing a purposeful helping method & client outcomes such as improved social relationships, individuals' performance of social roles, & personality characteristics. M. Richmond developed Loch's charitable framework into the concept of the social situation; described its various social situational components & relationships between them; & identified rudimentary helping & client social situations. Early social workers developed such a social situational approach into a purposeful social treatment of social diagnosis & intervention within the emerging field & discipline of social work. 53 References. Christian Womanist Spirituality: Implications for Social Work Practice

Author: Jackson, Margaret Ann11 Waccamaw Center Mental Health, Georgetown, SC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61483291?accountid=14667

Abstract: The womanist movement arises out of the African American historical & cultural experience, as well as in response to the feminist movement. Its relation to the feminist movement is discussed & its historical evolution is traced. It springs not only from the merging of African cosmology & Christianity, but also from the lived experience of African American women, who have endured a tridimensional form of oppression in which racism, sexism, & classism interact. Some of the implications of Christian womanist spirituality for social work practice are offered in the areas of both clinical practice & systemic issues. 21 References. Adapted from the source document.

Graduate Social Work Students' Attitudes about Client Religion

Author: DeCoster, Vaughn A1; Burcham, Scott1 Coll Social Work, U Tennessee, Memphis

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61472645?accountid=14667

Abstract: This paper describes a study that explored the attitudes of graduate students about client religion & social work practice. Findings suggest that students recognize the importance of religion yet are less sure how to operationalize this concern. Analysis across variables indicated that student religious affiliation & activity levels exerted more influence on these professional attitudes than social work education. 7 Tables, 1 Appendix, 37 References. Reflecting on Daily Experience: What Does Ignatian Spirituality Have to Offer Social Work Students?

Author: Staral, Janice M11 Dept Social & Cultural Sciences, Marquette U, Milwaukee, WI janice.staral@marquette.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61446454?accountid=14667

Abstract: This exploratory study considers whether social work students could benefit from learning about Ignatian Spirituality, which is central to the ideals of Catholic, Jesuit universities. Of specific concern is the prayer form of reflection & contemplation. Does this form help in decision making & self care in today's fast paced society & the pressures of doing social work? To answer this question, a Jesuit from Marquette U met with undergraduate students during a two-hour advanced social work seminar & linked concepts from Ignatian Spirituality to social work. Feedback about this experience was obtained through class discussion & an anonymous questionnaire. 52 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Future Is Aging

Author: Takamura, Jeanette C11 US Dept Health & Human Services, Honolulu, HI

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61530969?accountid=14667

Abstract: The social & moral meanings of aging & of being an older person are evolving within an increasingly global context. Although there are differences that can be drawn between developed & developing nations, these meanings appear to be differentiated by variables such as gender, race & ethnicity, living arrangements, & age cohort. However, the legitimacy or dominance accorded some of the meanings will likely be dependent upon the ideological beliefs of those who are deemed experts or who wield influence in policy circles. Meanwhile, the resolution of many of the most pressing aging policy issues will be compelled by the sheer demographics of aging & confounded by the extent to which ideological perspectives are intractable. 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

Conceptual Models of Spirituality

Author: Carroll, Maria M11 Dept Social Work, Delaware State U, Dover MCarrol@dsc.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61418222?accountid=14667

Abstract: The traditional social work view of human nature & the whole person has emphasized biological, psychological, & social dimensions. Interdisciplinary &, more recently, social work conceptualizations of the whole person have added spirituality. After exploring definitions of spirituality, this article describes seven models that include diagrams that enhance the conceptual understanding of spirituality. The models are examined with regard to the spiritual growth process by drawing on developmental theories. A new diagrammatic model, Spirituality: A Wholistic Model, illustrates the relationship between spirituality & the biological, psychological, social, & transpersonal dimensions of the person. It provides a way to evaluate the helpfulness of experiences, including practice interventions, with respect to their role in assisting each individual in moving toward realization of full potential. 7 Figures, 47 References. Adapted from the source document.

Transpersonal Psychology and Deep Ecological Philosophy: Exploring Linkages and Applications for Social Work

Author: Besthorn, Fred H11 Dept Social Work, Washburn U, Topeka, KS zzbest@washburn.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61493399?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article broadens the way social work understands the ways humanity defines & shapes its individual & collective realities in relation to nature. It incorporates & links relevant knowledge from transpersonal psychology & deep ecological philosophy in an effort to formulate fresh avenues for defining, pursuing, & resolving the many challenges that humankind faces at the dawn of this new millennium. The article concludes by suggesting some points of connection for generating a trans/ecological approach to social work & how this may portent important shifts of focus in social work theory & practice. 97 References. Adapted from the source document.

Retirement Patterns and Pension Policy: An International Perspective

Author: Hokenstad, M. C. "Terry"1; Johansson, Lennarth1 Mandel School Applied Social Sciences, Case Western Reserve U, Cleveland, OH

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61483490?accountid=14667

Abstract: Population aging & the changing nature of work are reshaping thinking about retirement in postindustrial society. The future will see less demarcation between the work & retirement phases of life. This will include a growing trend towards partial retirement & flexible retirement. Changes in pension policy will contribute to changing patterns of retirement. Recent US legislation has uncoupled retirement from Social Security. New policy in Sweden provides partial pensions for partial retirement. Other pension policy changes in the European Union also are contributing to the redefinition of retirement in the 21st century. Adapted from the source document.

Who Is Responsible for the Care of the Elderly? A Comparison of Policies in the United States, the United Kingdom, and Israel

Author: Cox, Carole11 Graduate School Social Service, Fordham U, New York, NY

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61445721?accountid=14667

Abstract: One of the most pressing issues in our society is that of deciding who is responsible for the care of the dependent elderly & how this responsibility should be shared among individuals, families, & government. Both the UK & Israel have developed policies that focus on community care & that recognize & support the roles of families as caregivers. By examining their systems, valuable insights may be learned that may contribute to the development of policies in the US. 27 References. Adapted from the source document.

Alleviating Suffering in the Face of Death: Insights from Constructivism and a Transpersonal Narrative Approach

Author: Smith, Elizabeth D11 National Catholic School Social Service, Catholic U America, Washington, DC smithe@cua.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61464340?accountid=14667

Abstract: Confronting one's mortality is at the heart of much human suffering. Building upon her previous development & testing of an exploratory model of psychospiritual distress, the author explores the confrontation of death in light of a transpersonal narrative with four new dimensions: (1) normalization of death, (2) divine intention, ie, a belief in a supernatural force of higher power that provides a cosmic order, (3) surrender, ie, the ability to let go of the outcome of events & to accept the unknown, & (4) transpersonal existence, ie, a belief in a continued existence beyond the known mortal self. Through a constructivist perspective on this transpersonal narrative, one can understand how personal reality is constructed & how affect flows from core beliefs that mediate events. This offers an explanatory model of how annihilation vulnerability of personhood can be mediated, resulting in diminished suffering. It suggests implications for practice to alleviate the actual suffering a person experiences. 34 References. Adapted from the source document.

Pakistan's Zakat System: A Policy Model for Developing Countries as a Means of Redistributing Income to the Elderly Poor

Author: Clark, Grace11 International Center Global Aging, National Catholic School Social Service, Catholic U America, Washington, DC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61482336?accountid=14667

Abstract: Pakistan's national zakat system is a simple welfare system based on traditional Islamic law. It provides minimal benefits to the very poorest of Pakistan's poor, especially the elderly. Although the system was launched with the highest religious ideals, utilizing creative approaches to collecting & disbursing zakat, over time this system has experienced deficiencies due to corruption, favoritism, & government greed. While zakat has not met the original goals of eliminating poverty or eliminating beggary, & while it has met the goals of providing rehabilitation & redistributing income in only the most modest sense, Pakistan has still demonstrated the potential for a zakat system to provide some cash income to the very poorest old in a very poor country who would otherwise have no cash income at all. 34 References. Adapted from the source document.

Transpersonalism and Social Work Practice: Awakening to New Dimensions for Client Self-Determination, Empowerment, and Growth

Author: Leight, Arlen Keith11 Transpersonal Psychotherapy of Washington, DC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61505335?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article proposes & advocates integration of a transpersonal model into clinical social work practice as a logical extension of the profession's inclusive perspective. The theory & practice of a transpersonal approach to psychotherapy & its applicability to social work are investigated, especially for use with marginalized populations. Transpersonalism is examined as an opportunity to enhance the worker's ability to respect & honor client self-determination, facilitate bio-psycho-social-spiritual growth & development, & empower even the most vulnerable in our society. 21 References. Adapted from the source document.

Cosmic Consciousness: Path or Pathology?

Author: Cowley, Au-Deane S

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61509621?accountid=14667

Abstract: Historically the relationship between spirituality & mental health has been characterized by confusion in terms of what constitutes healthy spirituality (path) as opposed to psychotic states (pathology). Finding criteria to help differentiate pre-rational structures from trans-rational structures (since they are both non-rational) has been an elusive goal. Ken Wilber's Full Spectrum of Consciousness Model, presented in 1986, is the only transpersonal theory that offers descriptors for three general levels of consciousness (prepersonal, personal, & transpersonal), the pathologies likely to develop at each level of development, as well as preferred interventions for developmental problems at each level of consciousness. This chapter applies Wilber's model & related ideas from other transpersonal theorists in order to provide differential assessment guidelines for therapists working with the spiritual dimension of clients' experience. 52 References. Adapted from the source document.

Religiosity as a Factor Affecting Adjustment of Minority Elderly to a Nursing Home

Author: Sasson, Sassy11 Jewish Home & Hospital, Bronx, NY

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60429389?accountid=14667

Abstract: This study examines the association between religiosity, adjustment, & satisfaction of nursing home residents in one long-term care facility. A sample of convenience was used to conduct face-to-face interviews of 71 Jewish & 21 African American alert residents age 65 & older. Various scales were utilized to measure resident adjustment & satisfaction, religious identity & level of involvement in religious activities. Additional information was compiled that provided a profile of the physical, mental, & social functions of each resident. The findings revealed that residents who exhibit higher levels of religiosity were likely to show higher levels of adjustment & satisfaction with nursing home living. However, the results lost their significance after controlling for a variety of other characteristics. The results suggest that the continuation of previous religious roles, activities, & behavior of nursing home residents may prompt increased satisfaction & a more successful adjustment to the long-term care setting. The implications of these findings for practice, program development, & future research will be discussed. 4 Tables, 37 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Relationship between Spiritual Development and Ethnicity in Violent Men

Author: Freeman, Dexter R11 Soldier & Family Support Branch, Army Medical Dept Center & School, Fort Sam Houston, TX dexfree@earthlink.net

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61468278?accountid=14667

Abstract: There is a dearth of empirically based literature on spirituality & how it impacts the behavior of violent men. In fact, domestic violence practitioners & researchers often diminish the influence of spirituality in the lives of violent men & assume that violent men, regardless of their ethnicity, can be accurately understood using Eurocentric paradigms that de-emphasize the importance of spirituality. This article reveals that the lack of attention that has been given to spirituality may be negating a significant resource for violent men, especially among African American men. It provides empirical data on the spiritual perspectives of African American & European American men. It also shows that the spiritual energies that promote a sense of wholeness have a significant influence on the level of physical violence used by violent men, regardless of their ethnic identity. 3 Tables, 35 References. Adapted from the source document.

Physical Dysfunction and Social Participation among Racial/Ethnic Groups of Older Americans: Implications for Social Work

Author: Bertera, Elizabeth M1; Bailey-Etta, Barbara1 Catholic U America, Washington, DC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60442452?accountid=14667

Abstract: This paper reports the findings of a study that was undertaken to (1) identify differences in social participation patterns among racial/ethnic & gender groups, (2) examine the association between physical dysfunction & church & club attendance, & (3) explore opportunities for social work interventions that improve the quality of life of older Americans. The study was based on a national sample representative of the 39 million Americans over age 60 The data indicate that those who attended both church & club meetings had the lowest levels of physical dysfunction; those who attended one but not the other had intermediate levels of dysfunction, & those who did not attend church & also did not attend club meetings had the highest dysfunction levels. These findings suggest that physical limitations reduce participation in social activities at church & in clubs, which may limit access to social support for older persons that could benefit the most from it. Social workers should seek ways of identifying natural support systems when working with older adults to help provide social participation opportunities for older persons, especially those that may have access & mobility problems due to physical limitations. 3 Tables, 37 References. Adapted from the source document.

Transcending through Disability and Death: Transpersonal Themes in Living with Cystic Fibrosis

Author: Canda, Edward R11 School Social Welfare, U Kansas, Lawrence edc@ukans.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61471881?accountid=14667

Abstract: This study examines transpersonal themes related to a sense of dealing with spiritual transcendence through disability & death as represented in the views of adults with cystic fibrosis (CF), a life threatening chronic hereditary disease. Analysis of online discussion, autobiographical writings, & interviews of 16 people with CF identified spiritual beliefs, spiritual metaphors, transpersonal developmental patterns, & accounts of transpersonal experiences, such as miracles & contact with sacred beings. The principles of empowerment & phenomenologically oriented research for transpersonal topics shaped the methodology of this qualitative study. Implications for spiritually sensitive social work practice with people with chronic illnesses are presented. 3 Tables, 67 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Logotherapeutic Approach to the Quest for Meaningful Old Age

Author: Guttman, David11 Faculty Welfare & Health Studies, U Haifa, Mount Carmel, Israel

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61529792?accountid=14667

Abstract: This article introduces logotherapy as a meaning centered psychotherapy & its relevance to social work with the aged. According to this theory, human beings are motivated first & foremost to finding meaning in life. Ways of discovering meaning are discussed along with Frankl's "tragic triad," consisting of guilt, suffering, & death. Each of these unavoidable factors in life offer opportunities for discovering meaning. The importance of spirituality in old age is stressed, & Cicero's Cato "the elder" is presented as a model for meaningful old age. 21 References. Adapted from the source document.

Aging, Religion, and Spirituality: Advancing Meaning in Later Life

Author: David, Gerson11 Graduate School Social Work, U Houston, TX

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61480988?accountid=14667

Abstract: We would not be relevant in the 21st century if we did not visit religion & spirituality in the field of aging. This essay first examines the ageist society & challenges its present mind-set to dispel ageism & engage in intervention designed to enhance quality of living. It next moves to a consideration of aging & meaning & the role of religion & spirituality in advancing meaning in later life. It concludes with a brief discussion of meaning making & soul-nourishment of the able-old & frail-old, affirming the value of spiritual development continuing throughout old age. 26 References. Adapted from the source document.

Addressing Spirituality in Hospice: Current Practices and a Proposed Role for Transpersonal Social Work

Author: Reese, Dona J11 Social Work Program, U Arkansas, Fayetteville reese@mail.uark.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61505421?accountid=14667

Abstract: Despite evidence of the importance of spirituality to terminally ill patients, the social work profession has developed few curriculum materials, practice models, or research on this topic. This chapter presents theoretical & empirical support for the proposition that transition to the transegoic stage of consciousness can promote a comfortable death for hospice patients & that hospice social workers should address spiritual issues in order to assist terminally ill patients & their families in making this transition. It also presents the results of a national survey describing & testing the effectiveness of some current social work approaches to addressing spirituality in hospice. Implications for practice & social work education are explored. 3 Tables, 58 References. Adapted from the source document.

Examining Role Change: A Qualitative Study of Catholic Sisters Who Became Family Caregivers

Author: Burke, JoAnn Meyer11 Dept Social Work & Anthropology, Saint Mary's Coll, Notre Dame, IN

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61482044?accountid=14667

Abstract: Women in Catholic religious institutes are members of organizations that prohibited family caregiving until the late 20th century. Forty-six women from 11 non-cloistered religious institutes participated in a qualitative study focused on understanding their parent care experiences from the perspective of role theory. Embedded in a society experiencing an era of extended longevity, the study participants appear to have expanded the role of Catholic sister to include the ministry of family elder care. 25 References. Transpersonal Social Work with Couples: A Compatibility-Intimacy Model

Author: Derezotes, David11 Graduate School Social Work, U Utah, Salt Lake City Dderezotes@socwk.utah.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61464383?accountid=14667

Abstract: A model of transpersonal couple work is described, which builds upon Wilber's (1986) seminal theory of transpersonal development & Berne's (1961) Transactional Analysis Theory. A practical plan of assessment & intervention is forwarded. Essentially, the worker first assesses the primary level of consciousness of both partners & then develops a strategy to help both partners move more fluidly into their other two available (but currently underdeveloped) consciousness states. 2 Figures, 22 References. Adapted from the source document.

Spirituality: Towards a Theoretical Framework

Author: Hodge, David R11 Washington U, St. Louis, MO DRHI@gwbmail.wust/.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61669288?accountid=14667

Abstract: Integrating existing theory & research, a theoretical framework of spirituality is created. Seven pathways are developed through which spirituality engenders a wide range of salutary outcomes. The seven pathways are health-promotive behaviors & lifestyles, social support, psychodynamics of ritual, psychodynamics of cognitive schemata, ego challenge, quantum effects, & supernatural effects. Practice & research implications that flow from the framework are discussed. 1 Figure, 88 References. Adapted from the source document.

Spiritual Well-Being, Population Aging, and a Need for Improving Practice with the Elderly: A Psychosocial Account

Author: Ai, Amy11 U Michigan, Ann Arbor

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61648378?accountid=14667

Abstract: To improve spiritual care for the elderly, influential psychosocial theories are reviewed in terms of their approaches to spiritual or religious issues & aging or adult development. Current theoretical advancements in this regard are introduced for improving social work practice with the elderly &, in turn, improving spiritual well-being. 52 References. Adapted from the source document.

Culture and Spirituality: A Review of Literature

Author: Ortiz, Larry1; Villereal, Sue; Engel, Margaret1 Worden School Social Service, Our Lady of the Lake U, San Antonio, TX

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61653187?accountid=14667

Abstract: Reports on a content analysis of social science literature that addresses spirituality & culture based on the review of the "fit" of 50+ articles in the social work curriculum. Most entries reviewed fit into the curricular areas of practice or human behavior in the social environment. It is concluded that most articles are relevant in more than one curricular area & will serve as a resource for social work faculty as they include content on spirituality as an aspect of diversity, according to the Council on Social Work Education's current Curriculum Policy statement. 72 References. Adapted from the source document.

Building a Spiritual Based Model to Address Substance Abuse

Author: Friedman, Bruce D11 School Social Work, Wayne State U, Detroit, MI

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61622007?accountid=14667

Abstract: Suggests that the low rate of substance abuse in the Jewish community is linked to a value orientation relying heavily on God, Torah, & Israel (community). These three concepts are used to help understand spirituality & how the interrelationship between the three are important in leading to low substance abuse rates. These components are generalized into the larger social service community in understanding the term spirituality. There seems to be a relationship between the interrelationship of God, Torah, & Israel with the concept of spirituality; development of a model based on this interaction is proposed as a way to reduce substance abuse. 32 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Building+a+Spiritual+Based+Model+to+Address+Substance+Abuse&amp;rft.au=Friedman%2C+Bruce+D&amp;rft.aulast=Friedman&amp;rft.aufirst=Bruce&amp;rft.date=2000-01-01&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=23&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Spirituality, Social Support, and Worry about Health: Relationships in a Sample of HIV+ Women

Author: Reese, Dona J1; Kaplan, Mark S1 Dept Social Work, U North Dakota, Grand Forks

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61623590?accountid=14667

Abstract: Examines the relationships between spirituality, social support, & worry about health through interviews of 53 ethnically diverse human immunodeficiency virus-positive (HIV+) women. Women reported coping with their disease primarily through spirituality & gave personal definitions of spirituality. Results indicate that both spirituality & social support have inverse relationships with worry about one's health, but the relationship between social support & worry disappears when controlling for spirituality & ethnicity. 3 Tables, 48 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Spirituality%2C+Social+Support%2C+and+Worry+about+Health%3A+Relationships+in+a+Sample+of+HIV%2B+Women&amp;rft.au=Reese%2C+Dona+J%3BKaplan%2C+Mark+S&amp;rft.aulast=Reese&amp;rft.aufirst=Dona&amp;rft.date=2000-01-01&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.spage=37&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Do Faith-Based Providers Respect Client Autonomy? A Comparison of Client and Staff Perceptions in Faith-Based and Secular Residential Treatment Programs

Author: Hodge, David R11 George Warren Brown School Social Work, Washington U, St. Louis, MO

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61642618?accountid=14667

Abstract: Explores client (N = 68 respondents, mean age 25.06) & staff (N = 48 respondents, mean age 30.84) views of autonomy, a fundamental social work value, by comparing perceptions at faith-based & secular residential treatment programs in the US. Based on a postmodern perspective that all organizations convey a particular set of values, & clients will tend to select programs congruent with their preexisting metaphysical values, it is hypothesized that there would be no difference in perceptions of autonomy among consumers or staff. Questionnaire data support both hypotheses, suggesting that for consumers who desire faith-based services, such providers do respect client autonomy. 3 Tables, 1 Figure, 45 References. Adapted from the source document.

Christian Welfare Ideologies: The Basis of Human Welfare

Author: Chan, Chak-Kwan1; Lap-Yan, Kung1 Social Work Program, Higher School Public Administration, Macau Polytechnic Instit chakkwanchan@ctimail.com

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61644381?accountid=14667

Abstract: Explores the nature of human welfare from Christian ideologies. It is found that pursuing human dignity, & promoting social fellowship & justice are ultimate goals of the Christian welfare approach. Thus, Christian values are likely to provide us an alternative ideological base for developing human welfare in the modern world. 39 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Spirit of Collaboration: Social Work/the Church/Older Adults

Author: Tirrito, Terry11 Coll Social Work, U South Carolina, Columbia terry.tirrito@sc.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61648430?accountid=14667

Abstract: In an era labeled the "devolution revolution," the challenge is to develop new paradigms of collaboration between churches & public/private agencies to meet the needs of church members & especially those of a growing population of older persons. Here, it is suggested that the integration of social work practice with theological principles to develop collaborative programs & services between churches & public/private agencies can benefit older adults & all members of society. 38 References. In Pursuit of a Living Wage: The Ethical and Economic Thought of Father John A. Ryan from the Late 1890s until the New Deal

Author: Francoeur, Richard Benoit11 School Social Work, U Pittsburgh, PA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61645933?accountid=14667

Abstract: Father Ryan frequently cited Pope Leo XIII's major encyclical, Rerum novarum (On the Condition of Labor), to lend the support of traditional Catholic social & labor reform in the US. Advocating "sane individualism," Ryan was the first American to argue convincingly that employers were bound in strict justice to pay employees at least a living wage, & his ethical influence gained wide appeal due to his conservative yet fair-minded approach to distributive justice. Ryan supported labor unions & economic planning as means to gain fair wages & stock ownership for all workers & emphasized income redistribution to reduce underconsumption druing the Depression. 48 References. Adapted from the source document.

Compassion, Solidarity and Empowerment: The Ethical Contribution of Religion to Society

Author: Coleman, John A11 Loyola Marymount U, Los Angeles, CA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61623234?accountid=14667

Abstract: Compassion, solidarity, & empowerment represent the three key anchors of Catholic social teaching; all three are interrelated. The concrete embodiment of compassion -- so as to remove sentimental vagueness from the concept -- entails the three-fold practices of direct social services, public advocacy, & strategies of empowerment. In particular, the Catholic notion of justice as participation looks to the active empowerment of those who are marginalized. Ultimately, welfare means more than merely providing for those in need, but enabling them to become active agents in society. Having sketched the social teaching, attention is given to sociological evidence about how well the churches practice what they preach. In our society, churches preeminently generate acts of compassion through voluntarism. Members of churches are more likely to give time & money to the voluntary sector than nonmembers are. One concrete program of empowerment is sketched: church-based community organizing. 21 References. Adapted from the source document.

Distributive Justice in the Workplace: Emerging Social Work Interventions

Author: Raber, Marie J1; Conrads, Ann Patrick1 NCSSS, Catholic U America, Washington, DC

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61656986?accountid=14667

Abstract: In the wake of recurrent corporate consolidations, downsizings, & restructuring, today's workers face increasing threats of job loss, job insecurity, & lack of employment opportunities. Examined here is how US business & the social work profession come to grips with the present workplace upheavals, displacement of workers, & the distributive justice implications to individuals & companies. Emphasis is placed on the historical development of the role of EAP (employee assistance program) social workers & their contributions to distributive justice in the workplace. Emerging from this discussion is a comprehensive model that integrates EAPs with organizational development based on the premise that a worker with strong self-esteem & reasonable expectation of continued employment is an indicator of a productive employee & an example of distributive justice in practice. 33 References. Adapted from the source document.

Welfare Reform and the Future of Foster Care

Author: Rome, Sunny Harris1; Slaght, Evelyn F1 George Mason U, Fairfax, VA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61654490?accountid=14667

Abstract: To document the impact of the Personal Responsibility & Work Opportunity Act of 1996 on the lives of children, interviews with key informants were conducted in Washington (DC), MD, & VA. Findings indicate that there is little quantitative data available, even in states like VA where welfare recipients are reaching the 2-year time limit for obtaining employment. In MD, data are only available on those leaving welfare early, & the impact there on the child welfare system is reported as minimal. The data focus on employment success & evade the effects of low wages, inadequate child-care availability, teenage parenting issues, kinship care, & inadequate services, especially for those with substance abuse, health, & mental health problems. Although quantitative data are limited, qualitative data indicate that the mandate of "personal responsibility" may become a mechanism for revoking our social commitment to protect children. 15 References. Adapted from the source document.

An Accountability Group: Case Study of a Church-Based Response to Sexual Abuse by Clergy

Author: Schmidt-Tieszen, Ada1; Canda, Edward R1 School Social Work, Bethel Coll, North Newton, KS

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61664392?accountid=14667

Abstract: Presents a case study of a method of responding to sexual abuse of parishioners by clergy in the Mennonite Church. The accountability group process attempts to hold the perpetrator accountable in an effort to achieve both justice & community restoration. Delinquency Prevention in Poor and At-Risk African-American Youth: A Social Work Practice Innovation

Author: Forster, Michael1; Rehner, Timothy1 U Southern Mississippi, Hattiesburg

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61664428?accountid=14667

Abstract: Describes the background, principles, program, & outcomes of the Family Network Partnership, a small community-based delinquency prevention program in Hattiesburg, MS. The program joins the city housing authority, community policing team, youth court, & local state university in efforts to address delinquency in a local public housing project. The program uses three primary strategies: (1) intervention with youth already involved with the juvenile justice system; (2) skill building among youth prior to court involvement; & (3) community capacity building. With qualification, the partnership is offered as a model for replication in similar communities. 59 References. Adapted from the source document.

Author: Schmitz, Cathryne L11 Graduate School Social Work, U Denver, CO cschmitz@du.edu

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61664937?accountid=14667

Child Caregiving by First-Time Fathers: Key Factors and Implications

Author: Zeiger, Spencer1; Andrews, Janice1 Social Work Dept, U Alaska, Anchorage

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61649051?accountid=14667

Abstract: Secondary analysis of data from a larger longitudinal study was conducted to explore the male experience of expectant & new parenthood, & men's caring needs over the prenatal period, as part of the family unit in transition. Interview data from 25 men collected from early pregnancy to 12 months postpartum are used to generate a substantive theory describing the projected range & level of paternal caregiving. Three core categories conceptualize the fathers' experience: how the power of the child reframes reality for first-time fathers; intrapersonal factors that influence paternal involvement; & interpersonal factors that influence paternal involvement. It is suggested that more fathers would become involved caregivers if they were given the requisite skills, societal opportunities, & social reinforcements. 3 Figures, 71 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Child+Caregiving+by+First-Time+Fathers%3A+Key+Factors+and+Implications&amp;rft.au=Zeiger%2C+Spencer%3BAndrews%2C+Janice&amp;rft.aulast=Zeiger&amp;rft.aufirst=Spencer&amp;rft.date=1999-01-01&amp;rft.volume=19&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=63&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Fostering Resiliency in Children: Lessons Learned in Transcending Adversity

Author: Palmer, Nancie11 Dept Social Work, Washburn U, Topeka, KS

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61623261?accountid=14667

Abstract: The centerpiece of this presentation is the Differential Resiliency Model (DRM), an original conceptual framework developed by the author to promote understanding of the process of "survival" & the development of resilience over time. Drawing on the DRM, practitioners & other helping advocates may more adequately & timely identify & intervene with appropriate resources. Approaching children in poverty & adversity with a new appreciation for their capacity & strengths may also enhance their growth to a level of thriving. It is not enough to settle for "survival" or a "good enough" quality of life. The ultimate test is enabling children & their families to thrive & flourish. It is the only acceptable standard of professional & social response. 1 Table, 1 Figure, 33 References. Adapted from the source document.

Refugee Children in Africa: Psychological Consequences of Displacement

Author: Bryant, Shirley1; Ahearn, Frederick L, Jr1 School Social Work, Virginia Commonwealth U, Falls Church

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61467281?accountid=14667

Abstract: In the context of expanding refugee populations worldwide, a comprehensive model for understanding refugee children is presented, focusing on Africa. The model addresses the psychological consequences of displacement utilizing the concepts of trauma & stress, social & emotional supports, loss & bereavement, & coping & adaptation. Emphasis is placed on the urgent need for involvement of the social work profession in relieving the suffering of these displaced children. 30 References. Adapted from the source document.

Ethics Consultation in Social Work

Author: Reamer, Frederic G11 School Social Work Rhode Island Coll, Providence 02908

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61585725?accountid=14667

Abstract: Although social workers have recently paid increased attention to ethical issues in the profession, social work has not yet cultivated a cadre of ethics consultants to assist practitioners who encounter ethical dilemmas. The development of ethics consultation in other professions is described, & a framework for ethics consultation in social work is presented. Particular attention is paid to the ethical issues on which social workers may find consultation useful, the settings in which ethics consultation should be offered, possible roles for ethics consultants, & the skills required for competent consultation. A case illustration is included, along with recommendations to enhance the development of ethics consultation in social work. 39 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Typological Model for the Assessment of Religious Groups

Author: Lewandowski, Cathleen A1; Canda, Edward R1 School Social Welfare U Kansas, Lawrence 66045

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61499020?accountid=14667

Abstract: A model to assist social workers' assessment of psychosocial impact on clients resulting from participation in various types of religious groups is described that avoids judgmental or ethnocentric assumptions. Rather than evaluating beliefs, the model develops a typology of religious groups based on specific organizational characteristics related to leadership & member recruitment styles. The possible psychosocial impacts on members, resulting from these styles & other organizational culture characteristics, are considered. The model is based on a value commitment to respect religious diversity while acknowledging the need for assessment guidelines in practice. 1 Figure, 39 References. Adapted from the source document.

Spirituality and Religiosity in Practice: In-Depth Interviews of Social Work Practitioners

Author: Derezotes, David S1; Evans, Kathleen E1 Graduate School Social Work U Utah, Salt Lake City 84112

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61499048?accountid=14667

Abstract: Attitudes of social workers in UT (N = 56) toward spiritual & religious issues in practice were examined via in-depth interviews. Several key themes emerged: (1) spirituality & religiosity are different issues, but both should be considered in working with all client populations; (2) formal training for social workers currently does not provide the knowledge & skills required for practice with spiritual & religious issues; (3) social workers need to understand their own beliefs & biases about spirituality & religiosity & tend to their own spiritual growth; & (4) spiritual & religious content can be integrated into existing social work curricula. 2 Figures, 37 References. Adapted from the source document.

Integrating and Transcending Divorce: A Transpersonal Model

Author: Smith, Elizabeth D1; Gray, Cathleen1 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61619456?accountid=14667

Abstract: Because many Western psychologies fail to recognize spirituality & transcendental needs as intrinsic aspects of human nature, they may not be meeting the needs of those experiencing psychospiritual distress due to divorce. There is a growing recognition among clinicians that current divorce models of intervention may not meet the needs of this population in that they tend to ignore spiritual or transpersonal dimensions. To move entirely beyond the pathogenic & reactive grief models of divorce, an emergent growth model of transpersonal development is presented. This model has eight phases of intervention & has been adapted for use with divorcing clients. 33 References. Adapted from the source document.

Rethinking "Ethnic Pride"

Author: Barbaro, Fred11 School Social Work Adelphi U, Garden City NY 11530

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61512771?accountid=14667

Abstract: Among the theories put forth as a model of assimilation for the diverse immigrant populations that have entered the US, cultural pluralism became the theory of choice in the 1960s, resulting in ethnically determined government policies & programs. While in the short run, some individuals in some groups benefited from pursuing separatist strategies, cultural diversity has done nothing to lessen discrimination or alleviate poverty, & it may be the major retardant of the welfare state. Cooperative strategies & a return to national goals stressing integration are proposed. 42 References. Adapted from the source document.

Modeling Organizational Culture in Catholic Social Services

Author: Maiello, Michael J

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61634351?accountid=14667

Abstract: A study of the influence that prevalent sociocultural models have on the organizational culture of Catholic social service agencies. The Catholic Worker Movement's solidarity with the poor is described as an example of how strong organizational cultures promote particular identifications. Domesticating, corporate, & liberationist cultural models are analyzed & critiqued. The effect these models have on the principal areas of organizational administration & operation -- governance, human resources management, management structure, program development, & public relations, & development -- are described, & recommendations made to facilitate the development of organizational cultures that are genuinely expressive of gospel values & that authentically realize the Church's mission of charity & justice. 18 References. Adapted from the source document.

Just Compensation: Application and Implication of Catholic Social Teaching

Author: Schervish, Philip H11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61317468?accountid=14667

Abstract: Social teachings of the Catholic church related to just compensation are examined, & applied to the current socioeconomic situation in the US. Statistical & census data are utilized to develop a new definition for poverty & populations at risk, suggesting that 30% of the US population may fall below poverty level. Church leaders & social workers are called to renew efforts to affect social policy initiatives for populations at risk. A policy agenda for the 1992 elections & beyond is proposed. 1 Table, 4 Figures, 11 References. Adapted from the source document.

Before Rerum Novarum: A Moral Theologian's View of Catholic Social Movements in 1891

Author: Nuesse, C Joseph11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61318080?accountid=14667

Abstract: The historical & theoretical antecedents of the papal encyclical Rerum Novarum issued in May 1891 are explored through the translation of an analysis undertaken shortly after the issuance by Thomas Joseph Bouquillon, a Belgian professor of moral theology at the Catholic U of America (Washington, DC). The survey & commentary, focusing on existing Catholic social movements in Europe, revealed the difficulty in foreseeing the profound effects that the encyclical would have. Bouquillon's perceptions into the French-Belgian debate about state intervention in the economy at the time encouraged leaders of European movements that have since been acknowledged as forerunners. In retrospect, the support of state intervention to secure the rights & welfare of workers in the new industrial order was a contemporary application of an inherited principle in Catholic social teaching. Bouquillon's memorandum reveals three sources of controversy about the application of the principle among European Catholics of its time. In the New World, the encyclical was welcomed for its defense of the right of private property as against socialism. Rerum Novarum ultimately held more significance for its recognition of the right of labor to organize than for its support of state interventions. Bouquillon's document portrays the dynamism of movements that are likely to seem more single-minded than they were, & evidences the contributions of those whose responses to the advance of industrialization were more traditional. 65 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocabsshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Before+Rerum+Novarum%3A+A+Moral+Theologian%27s+View+of+Catholic+Social+Movements+in+1891&amp;rft.au=Nuesse%2C+C+Joseph&amp;rft.aulast=Nuesse&amp;rft.aufirst=C&amp;rft.date=1991-01-01&amp;rft.volume=17&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=5&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Ethical Problem Solving Skills in Social Work Practice

Author: Conrad, Ann Patrick1; Joseph, M Vincentia1 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61310174?accountid=14667

Abstract: Data from questionnaires mailed to 58 field instructors in a school of social work in the northeastern US are used to explore how ethical issues are dealt with in clinical social work practice. Significantly, practitioners rarely used ethical skills to identify & resolve ethical conflict, & most often used lay or technical practice skills. These findings point to the need for the inclusion of ethical tools in the role coping repertoire of the practitioner, & to the importance of preparation for ethical problem solving in social work education. Implications for agencies in planning staff development programs in this area are noted. 1 Table, 20 References. Adapted from the source document.

Child Abuse and the Courts: Is McMartin the Best We Can Do?

Author: Jacobson, Wendy E11 Kirkwood Mental Health Center, Atlanta GA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61611149?accountid=14667

Abstract: A review of several of the social & systemic factors that have contributed to the increasingly prevalent crime of child abuse & its "cultural phenomenon" aspects. Focus is placed on the specific constitutional & procedural issues currently under debate in the search for a better way of handling child abuse cases in the court system. Child witness advocates & defendants alike are calling for changes that will help prevent system-induced victimization, but these two parties often formulate mutually exclusive solutions. Examination of their arguments leads to the conclusion that although the debate is often heated, there is enough underlying consensus between both sides to begin the process of change. Areas of agreement are described, & possible approaches based on education & multidisciplinary teamwork suggested. 31 References. Adapted from the source document.

International Adoption: The Solution or the Problem?

Author: Vitillo, Robert J11 Caritas Internationalis, Vatican City Italy

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61649651?accountid=14667

Abstract: An analysis of issues underlying international adoption practices, the attitudes of adoptive parents, & related views & positions of the Catholic Church, citing positive as well as negative experiences, & describing current trends. Basic theological, legal, & social work principles are drawn on to guide a deeper reflection on these issues. A continuum of service is posited as a framework for good intercountry adoption practices, with services carried out by professionally licensed & adequately monitored adoption agencies. An emphasis on development-oriented family-preservation interventions is recommended. A new model of church-based international child welfare services is presented as a means to address the complex needs inherent in international adoption. 14 References. The Church and Race Relations: Drawing Hope from a Deeper Well

Author: Ricard, John

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61284210?accountid=14667

Abstract: The response of the US Catholic church to the unique challenge that African Americans present to church social teaching is explored. Although the church's involvement in race relations & the struggle for racial equality became more visible during the 1960s, the church is not generally viewed as a longstanding advocate of racial justice. Examined are the impact that the slave system had on the church, how the church influenced the treatment of slaves, the spiritual well-being of slaves, & Catholic participation in slavery. The church's social teaching expressed in Pope Leo XIII's Rerum Novarum encyclical (1892), as well as other aspects of Catholic social thought, is investigated by focusing on black & white Catholic leaders who sought to raise the consciousness of fellow Catholics. The discussion addresses current efforts by church hierarchy & others to apply the heritage of church social teaching (eg, through pastoral letters on race) to the contemporary issues of racism, poverty, & discrimination. It is concluded that the church can no longer be content with issuing proclamations & declaring the moral high ground, & that it must identify & address obstacles to implementing its social vision. 27 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocabsshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=The+Church+and+Race+Relations%3A+Drawing+Hope+from+a+Deeper+Well&amp;rft.au=Ricard%2C+John&amp;rft.aulast=Ricard&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.date=1991-01-01&amp;rft.volume=17&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=25&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Narrative, Knowledge, and Professional Practice

Author: Holland, Thomas P11 School Social Work U Georgia, Athens 30602

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61651194?accountid=14667

Abstract: A treatise on the usefulness of narrative analysis (viewed as hermeneutical) as a methodological practice for social workers. It is argued that greater sensitivity to the themes & issues underlying practice problems, especially their ethical dimensions, can be developed by reflecting on the stories that people tell about themselves & others. Narratives serve to link inner & outer experiences & give them coherence & purpose. While the scientific method is useful in developing abstract or propositional knowledge, it is limited as a resource for helping practitioners to understand human consciousness, particularly questions of value & meaning that are often central to intervention. The latter goals can better be achieved through reflective analysis of narratives. Careful attention to the themes & patterns of values in life histories, case studies, & biographical material can stimulate greater moral awareness & provide the grounds for more responsible professional practice. 44 References. Adapted from the source document.

Psychosocial Coping of Urban Children in Catholic Elementary School Classrooms

Author: Sabatino, Christine Anlauf1; Timberlake, Elizabeth M; Zajicek-Farber, Michaela L1 School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61661662?accountid=14667

Abstract: An exploratory survey of kindergarten & first-grade children attending inner-city vs affluent Catholic schools in Washington, DC, based on questionnaire & other data obtained from 723 students & their teachers &/or principals covering demographic characteristics & children's psychosocial coping patterns, & leading to comparisons by school grouping. Chi square & analyses of variance yielded statistically significant differences: lower-income inner-city neighborhoods had more children who were younger, African-American, & living with one parent, & fewer who were Catholic. Children in inner-city schools demonstrated more classroom behavioral assets supporting learning & fewer behavior vulnerabilities inhibiting the process. Fewer inner-city children were identified as having "many" behavior problems, though more had "some" problems than was the case in more affluent schools. Implications of these findings are considered for future program development in school social work service provision. 4 Tables, 23 References. Adapted from the source document.

Poverty and the Church: Charity and the Preferential Option for the Poor

Author: Plionis, Elizabeth Moore11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61280755?accountid=14667

Abstract: An examination of whether assistance or charity (caritas) unwittingly institutionalizes the poverty it seeks to redress, exploring the theoretical & methodological underpinnings of the church's preferential option for the poor. An alternative explication of this option is developed by linking the methodology of nonviolence to symbolic interaction theory in order to bring about economic & sociopolitical change. Aimed at both personal & structural change, this perspective can redress the violence inherent in unjust systems without itself inflicting violence or denying the need at hand. 21 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Condition of Labor Today -- In the Light of One Hundred Years of Catholic Social Teaching

Author: Higgins, George G11 Dept Theology Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61307465?accountid=14667

Abstract: Many critics of Pope Leo XIII's Rerum Novarum (1891), as well as more recent papal encyclicals, have argued that these documents pay too much attention to the distribution of wealth & not enough to the need for greater productivity. These critics, however, are loathe to say that the distribution of wealth remains a serious problem, even in the most advanced industrial nations. An examination of Rerum Novarum in its historical context illuminates the fact that the encyclical was received differently in different nations because of their unique histories & traditions. In focusing on the issue of trade unionism & church-labor relations in the US, it is suggested that Rerum Novarum promoted unionism & collaboration between US Catholicism & the labor movement. Such involvement, however, gradually declined after the Vietnam War when religious & lay leaders turned their attention to pressing social & economic problems. Many believe that church-related agencies could impact the present crisis in the labor movement by reaffirming their support for strong & effective unions. A call is made for new & creative forms of labor-management cooperation, & for federal labor legislation that outlaws the growing practice of permanently replacing workers invovled in a legitimate strike. It is suggested that, despite the ethical & human problems at stake, the church may fail to recognize that it is made up of immigrants who need & deserve its sympathetic support of workers & their unions. 11 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Failure of Our Current View of Crime

Author: Sheedy, Patrick D11 Dept Theology Coll Saint Catherine, Saint Paul MN 55105

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61314721?accountid=14667

Abstract: It is argued that, as a society, we uncritically embrace a view of crime & punishment that is unworkable & flawed. By isolating & identifying the offender as the villain, the offender is alienated from society, & the conditions that contribute to crime remain unaddressed. It is suggested that the model of addiction more adequately illuminates the phenomenon of crime, & encourages a response to crime that is both individual & communal, ie, the formation of communities of honesty & compassion based on the twelve-step program of Alcoholics Anonymous. These communities would enable identification of personal & communal biases/sins regarding crime & punishment. 27 References. Adapted from the source document.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocabsshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=The+Failure+of+Our+Current+View+of+Crime&amp;rft.au=Sheedy%2C+Patrick+D&amp;rft.aulast=Sheedy&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrick&amp;rft.date=1991-01-01&amp;rft.volume=17&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.spage=43&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

The Legal Rights of Children in the United States

Author: Lewis, Mary R11 Graduate School Social Work U Houston, University Park TX 77004

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61284927?accountid=14667

Abstract: Major shifts in the legal rights of US children, the social forces precipitating the shifts, & the implications for children, their families, members of the helping professions, & child advocates are discussed. The state has become more directly involved in examining financial support & health care issues concerning children. Juvenile status-based institutions are receiving closer supervision by legislatures & courts in attempts to address the needs of children more fairly while respecting parental rights. Individual rights of children are being legislated or recognized by courts in limited ways in public schools, juvenile courts, & the child welfare system. 32 References. Adapted from the source document.

Questioning the Efficacy of One Hundred Years of Catholic Social Teaching: The Intrinsic Connection between Faith and Justice

Author: Nash, James Lyman11 Dept Religion & Religious Education Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61292664?accountid=14667

Abstract: Questions regarding the meaning & value that Catholic social teaching has had in history, as well as its future role, are raised. Topics explored include: the immediate purpose of the tradition of Catholic social teaching, the specific solutions that such teaching examines, its intended audience, & its effectiveness in altering the way people live. It is presupposed that this tradition has evolved historically, making answers to the inquiry tentative. It is contended that in order to accurately assess & interpret the tradition of Roman Catholic social teaching, the inseparable connection between action on behalf of justice & the demands of fidelity to the Gospel must be considered. It is concluded that: the church must integrate social justice into its liturgical life, the need to unite faith & justice on a personal & structural level must be recognized, & both the documents of the tradition & the church's liturgical life must directly address & empower the poor. 23 References. Adapted from the source document.

Protecting the Potential Victim of Sexual Violence: An Ethical Issue in Residential Care

Author: Kopfensteiner, Thomas R11 Kenrick-Glennon Theological Seminary, Saint Louis MO

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61656315?accountid=14667

Abstract: Because of social & familial backgrounds, many females in residential care are at high risk of sexual victimization. Two goals must be kept in proper balance in dealing with the victims or potential victims of sexual violence: (1) necessary steps should be taken to prevent a possible pregnancy that may result from sexual violence, which may mean the prescription of anovulant pills for those believed to be at risk; (2) counseling & education should be provided to lessen the adolescent's vulnerability to sexual victimization. 52 References. A Collaborative Model for Parish Social Ministry

Author: Hoff, Marie D11 School Social Service Saint Louis U, MO 63103

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61271899?accountid=14667

Abstract: Four central city Catholic parishes developed a collaborative social ministry organization to respond to the needs of their impoverished community. A case study desribes how 4 central city Catholic parishes in Saint Louis, Mo, developed a collaborative social ministry organization to respond to the needs of their impoverished community. Key elements of this successful endeavor include widespread parish volunteer participation in activities & policy making, & a model of ministry that integrates direct services, community education, community development, & social action. The collaborative efforts have promoted lay leadership & expanded vision of Christian community among the parishes & into the surrounding neighborhoods. 2 Figures, 24 References. Adapted from the source document.

Family, Work, and Culture: Postmodern Themes for Catholic Spirituality in Transforming the Crisis of Modernity

Author: Holland, Joe11 Saint Thomas U, Miami FL 33054

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61291451?accountid=14667

Abstract: Portrayed is a destructive, late-modern cultural battle over family & work, fueled by the advent of TV, carried on between liberalism's Right & Left wings. It is argued that the crisis of family & work stems in part from strains in Western classical spirituality, which modernity then developed technologically & psychologically. By contrast, a postmodern cultural vision of regeneration is proposed that offers a fresh & holistic synthesis of creative communion, expressed ecologically, socially, & spiritually, & focused in the sacred lay experiences of family & work. 1 Table. Social Forces and the Future of Catholic Schools

Author: Byron, William J11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61267553?accountid=14667

Abstract: An overview of the social forces affecting Catholic schools at all levels & their impact on the future of Catholic education. The development of Catholic education in the US is traced in relation to mission, the changing values of society, social status of Catholics, role of the community, religious pluralism, & the First Amendment to the Constitution. The teaching mission of the Church is discussed in relation to the quality of & support for Catholic education, canon Law, & the role of the theologian. If quality at all levels is achieved & maintained, support will follow & Catholic education will survive. 1 Illustration, 5 References. Adapted from the source document.

A Typology of Research Knowledge for Relating Research to Social Work Practice

Author: Tripodi, Tony11 U Pittsburgh, PA 15260-0001

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61653865?accountid=14667

Abstract: A typology of research knowledge pertinent to social work practice is proposed that consists of three major categories: substantive research knowledge, methodological research knowledge, & combined substantive & methodological knowledge. Each category subsumes several subcategories organized on two dimensions necessary for the practitioner's use of research, ie, time & skill. Prospects & limitations for the utilization of research are discussed, & suggestions are made for the further integration of research. 1 Figure, 83 References. Adapted from the source document.

Social Work and Employee Assistance Programs: Emerging Issues

Author: Cunningham, Gloria11 School Social Work Loyola U, Chicago IL 60611

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61290820?accountid=14667

Abstract: As a field of practice, occupational social work has been greatly influenced by identification with employee assistance programs & their typical focus on the chemically addicted employee. It is contended that this merger of two separate service models requires a clarification of roles & functions & a redefinition of the problem focus & treatment options in contemporary, work-based programs. An argument is made for an inclusive problem focus that considers a broader array of problems in human functioning, the increased complexity of chemical addictions, & an expansion of treatment options. 17 References. Adapted from the source document.

Knowledge as Experience: Exploring New Dimensions of Social Work Inquiry

Author: Weick, Ann11 School Social Welfare U Kansas, Lawrence 66045

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61299835?accountid=14667

Abstract: It is argued that the empiricist paradigm has narrowed the range of knowledge considered as a legitimate base for social work practice. To reclaim a broader view, several strategies for reconceptualizing the boundaries of human experience are proposed so as to incorporate tacit, intuitive ways of knowing. Principles deriving from this conception are offered as guides for a different kind of inquiry for social work. 1 Photograph, 46 References. Adapted from the source document.

Religion and Racism in South Africa: Conflict between Faith and Culture

Author: Lafferty, John

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61285082?accountid=14667

Abstract: The historical development of a racist ideology in South Africa, including the role of the South African version of Calvinism, is used to demonstrate how Christianity, though theologically opposed to racism, can be used in ethnocentrism or racism. A sociological analysis of religion, in addition to a theological analysis, is needed to understand how ideology constitutes a symbolic set of meanings that organize a culture. These analyses can help those within the church & the social work professional become more aware of subtle dynamics of cultural racism. 1 Illustration, 19 References. Adapted from the source document.

Stop the World, I Want to Stay On: Rationing Health Care, First the Aged, and Then?

Author: Abels, Paul1; Rice, Susan1 Dept Social Work California State U, Long Beach 90840

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61626013?accountid=14667

Abstract: An exploration of the growing effort to limit health services to the aged in the US, drawing on Daniel Callahan's Setting Limits: Medical Goals in an Aging Society (New York: Simon & Schuster, 1987). His three-part plan to limit health care is summarized, & the implications for society are discussed, including the quest for, & view of, a just society, the future as a moral community, & the impact on practice for helping professionals. Action is urged to address the moral consequences of such a plan. 19 References. Adapted from the source document.
