Job Satisfaction and Job Stress among African-American Human Service Workers

Author: Brabson, Howard V1; Jones, Charles A; Jayaratne, Srinika D1 U Michigan, Ann Arbor 48109

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61600236?accountid=14667

Abstract: Data gathered via questionnaire from 123 African-American social workers are drawn on to determine factors that cause job stress, & those that contribute to job satisfaction. Multiple regression analysis indicates that job satisfaction, burnout, & intention to change jobs were related only in terms of causal attributes. Also, promotion opportunities & role conflict predicted both job satisfaction & job turnover intent. Though discrimination was a predictor of job satisfaction, it was not found to be a factor in turnover. Implications of these findings are discussed, especially aspects that could be improved by human service agencies. 3 Tables, 1 Figure, 1 Appendix, 31 References. S. Dilts

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Job+Satisfaction+and+Job+Stress+among+African-American+Human+Service+Workers&amp;rft.au=Brabson%2C+Howard+V%3BJones%2C+Charles+A%3BJayaratne%2C+Srinika+D&amp;rft.aulast=Brabson&amp;rft.aufirst=Howard&amp;rft.date=1990-01-01&amp;rft.volume=16&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=47&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Family and Nation Revisited

Author: Moynihan, Daniel Patrick11 464 Russell Bldg, Washington DC 20510-0001

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61314373?accountid=14667

Abstract: Examined is the current condition of families & children in the US, arguing that establishing social policy conducive to the stability & well-being of family life will necessitate an honest effort to remedy such difficult issues as family structure, drugs, poverty, & race. Also, fiscal policies must be addressed & the findings of social science research taken more seriously if the plight of families is to be ameliorated. Specific directives are enumerated & discussed, including a call for the continued efforts of the Catholic Charities movement, which supports family life through the provision of services, & support of public policy based on reason & religious tradition. 1 Table, 2 Photographs, 19 References. Adapted from the source document.

Families and Government: Implementing a Family Perspective in Public Policy

Author: Ooms, Theodora

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61314428?accountid=14667

Abstract: Argued for is a redirection of research, discussion, & writing about family policy. It is maintained that too much attention has been given to the content of policy (ie, the need for a comprehensive national family policy) & too little to the processes involved in policy making. The most crucial challenge is how best to encourage a family perspective in the development, implementation, & monitoring of policy making at all government levels. It is warned that if policy making does not become family-focused, the current progress in family policy is likely to halt. The implementation of a family perspective in public policy making would include: an awareness of the impact of changes in family life on the major institutions of society, & a sensitivity to the fact that policies & programs can have varied effects on different types of families. An outline of the recent history of interest in family policy is given, & principles by which to evaluate public policies & programs from a family perspective are presented. 2 Photographs, 29 References. Adapted from the source document.

The Social Work Ethic

Author: Siporin, Max11 State U New York, Albany 12203

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61579798?accountid=14667

Abstract: The social work ethic expresses the function of social work in a society. Social work practice is understood as a moral enterprise, helping people with conflicts & dilemmas. Trends in the profession with regard to commitment to the mental health & civil rights movements, as well as no entrepreneurial forms of practice, have had positive & negative consequences for the ethical commitment of social work. The current moral & religious revival is potentially a corrective trend, though there is a need to safeguard its positive contributions. 1 Photograph, 36 References. HA

Toward Ethical Practice: The Relevance of Ethical Theory

Author: Reamer, Frederic G11 School Social Work Rhode Island Coll, Providence 02908

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61593865?accountid=14667

Abstract: In recent years, social workers have begun to explore the use of ethical theory to analyze ethical issues in practice. An overview is provided of traditional schools of thought in moral philosophy, & their relevance to social work practice is examined. Although ethical theory may not provide unequivocal answers to complex moral questions, it can provide a rigorous framework for the analysis of ethical dilemmas in social work. 2 Photographs, 19 References. Some Developments in Catholic Moral Theology and Their Promise for Social Workers

Author: Ryle, Edward J

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61436641?accountid=14667

Abstract: Catholic moral theology has changed in three major ways since Vatican II: the shift from classical to historical consciousness, from physicalism to the person, & from study of abstract human nature to concrete human nature influenced by history & culture. Implications of these shifts for moral judgment are discussed from a liberation theology perspective, & illustrated by three issues of ethical import & interest to social workers: (1) contraception, (2) homosexual marriages, & (3) the distribution of income in the US. It is suggested that the three changes in moral theology offer helpful resources for Catholic social workers & agencies. 1 Table, 1 Photograph, 38 References. HA

Individual & Organizational Ethics

Author: Smith, Joan M11 School Social Service Saint Louis U, MO 63103

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61571896?accountid=14667

Abstract: The interaction of the National Assoc of Social Workers (NASW) Code, dealing with individual ethics, & the Catholic Charities USA (CCUSA) Code, dealing with organization ethics, is examined in reference to compatibility & conflict. A major difference lies in the purpose of the codes: the NASW Code is prescriptive, while the CCUSA Code is normative. Ethics represents the translation of values into action & both codes identify the value of the person as fundamental. However, whereas the CCUSA Code identifies & elaborates the biblical & natural law source of basic values, the NASW does not qualify these values by suggesting source or context. Two dimensions of difference in the codes emerge as particularly significant: the social ethics-individual ethics dimension & the religious-secular dimension. 1 Photograph, 28 References. HA

Developing an Ethics Review Process in a Social Service Agency

Author: Conrad, Ann Patrick11 School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/1463023996?accountid=14667

Abstract: Ethics review committees have become important mechanisms for ethical decision making in the field of health care & have begun to emerge in social work settings. The health care experience is reviewed, & its implications for the development of processes for ethical reflection & decision making in social service agencies are considered. The design of explicit models for ethics review in social work should contribute to the integrity of the profession & its accountability to the community. 2 Photographs, 50 References. HA

AIDS: Confidentiality and the Social Worker

Author: Goldberg, Joan E

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61598057?accountid=14667

Abstract: The acquired immune deficiency syndrome (AIDS) epidemic presents a number of ethical dilemmas to those working with AIDS victims & their families. Discussed is the dilemma a social worker faces with a client susceptible to the AIDS virus: should a therapist maintain the ethical principle of confidentiality or should he/she breach that confidentiality in order to protect a third party from harm? A model of ethical resolution is offered that considers professional ethics, values, relevant information, & ethical options. 1 Photograph, 24 References. HA

Author: Summers, Anne B11 Arkansas Coll, Batesville 72501

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61551185?accountid=14667

Abstract: An exploration of the potential use of the concept of informed consent for eliciting some middle range theories to assist social workers in developing better focus & clarity about the meaning of client autonomy & self-determination. Ethics Curricula: A National Survey of Graduate Schools of Social Work

Author: Black, Phyllis N1; Hartley, Elizabeth Kennedy; Whelley, Joanne; Kirk-Sharp, Cordelia1 Graduate School Social Work Marywood Coll, Scranton PA 18509

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/1463023579?accountid=14667

Abstract: A mail survey of 102 US graduate schools of social work revealed that the predominant method for teaching ethical subject matter is through the pervasive/infusion approach, whereby ethical content is interwoven into the fabric of all or selected courses. Few programs use a discrete model in which professional ethical principles & decision making are the focus of a separate course. Analysis of syllabi of 6 discrete ethics courses showed considerable variation in content & lack of systematic organization. Given the present concern with ethical issues in practice, there is serious question concerning the efficacy of current methods of instruction for preparing students for ethical practices. 5 Tables, 28 References. HA

The Social Construction of Personhood

Author: Burkhart, Julia11 Dept Sociology/Social Work/Geography Arkansas State U, Jonesboro 72401

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61239974?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of the current controversy over abortion in the US, focusing on social aspects of personhood. Social groups & individuals determine whether a fetus is a person, & this in turn determines whether it is aborted or delivered. The definition of person is discussed from philosophical, legal, & medical viewpoints. The social ramifications of depersonalization are demonstrated through case examples of slavery & the Holocaust. 1 Illustration, 43 References. S. G. Yates

Common Themes and Polarities in Social Work Practice Theory Development

Author: Constable, Robert1; Cocozzelli, Carmelo1 School Social Work Loyola U, Chicago IL 60611

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61592355?accountid=14667

Abstract: Implicit in the development of social work practice theory have been common themes around the social worker's focus on the person-environment transaction, & on persons as subjects &/or objects (recipients) of the helping process. Both an analytic review of practice theory development & research on the operating assumptions of practitioners confirm these as lasting themes & also as polarities underlying theory development. Around these polarities different working philosophies of practice are clustered. They are reconcilable in the theoretically elaborated concept of "work.". 48 References. HA

Family Structure in the USSR: A Multidimensional Analysis

Author: Imbrogno, Salvatore11 Coll Social Work Ohio State U, Columbus 43210

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61228918?accountid=14667

Abstract: The role of the state in directing social norms & values is examined offering a case study of norms concerning marriage & family structure in the USSR. Three forms of family structure outlined in the 1977 revised Constitution are discussed: traditional, collective, & autonomous. Ways that societal values conflict with individual choice are analyzed, citing examples of multicultural marriage, divorce, shifting family structure, & abortion. It is concluded that increased urbanization, opportunities for women, & changing family dynamics have changed social norms, which, in turn, have altered the government's influence on family life. 21 References. S. G. Yates

Unfinished Business: Community Economic Development and the U.S. Catholic Bishops' Economic Pastoral

Author: Corbin, Brian R11 Dept Social Action Office Catholic Charities, Youngstown OH

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61249589?accountid=14667

Abstract: Various economic development models & strategies are evaluated in light of Catholic social teaching. It is argued that community-based models are the most appropriate, as they synthesize existing models & most closely follow the mandate prescribed in the US Catholic bishops' 1986 Pastoral Letter on the Economy. Major themes contained in this letter -- creation, covenant, community, subsidiarity, & social justice -- are discussed in relation to development. 1 Illustration, 29 References. S. G. Yates

Spirituality, Faith, and Social Change: A Case Study of Vida Dutton Scudder

Author: Faver, Catherine A11 Coll Social Work U Tennessee, Knoxville 37996

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61234351?accountid=14667

Abstract: Vida Dutton Scudder (1861-1954) was a professor at Wellesley Coll (Mass), a social activist, an Episcopal churchwoman, & a Christian socialist. Selections from autobiographical & other writings, as well as secondary biographical sources, are used to analyze the nature of her spirituality & social philosophy. Scudder believed that constructive social change requires both radical restructuring of the social order & moral transformation of individuals. Three principles inherent in her worldview that supported her social activism & undergirded her philosophy of social change are identified: (1) paradox is in the nature of ultimate reality; (2) God, rather than self, is the source of love; & (3) all living beings are vitally connected. 7 Photographs, 30 References. AA

Moral Theory for Social Work

Author: Imre, Roberta Wells11 Social Work Dept Seton Hall U, South Orange NJ 07079

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61539484?accountid=14667

Abstract: Focus is on the need to develop ethical theory appropriate to the moral nature of social work practice. Common ethical theories originating in the traditions of philosophy are considered to be limited as guides to practice decisions. Instead, a perspective is proposed in which caring is recognized as a primary underlying good -- a good integrally related to justice, which has consistently been recognized as a professional value in social work. Feminist thought & virtue theory are discussed as resources in the effort to clarify these issues, which are seen to be embedded in the nature of practice itself. 21 References. HA

Values, Faith and Professional Practice

Author: Holland, Thomas P11 School Social Work U Georgia, Athens 30602

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61467543?accountid=14667

Abstract: Commitments to certain values lie at the foundation of every profession & serve to shape the individual roles & careers of its practitioners. These values are expressed or represented in ideal images of what constitutes true worth, power, & meaning in the lives of participants. The profession of social work began in the nineteenth century with some religious commitments that often placed it in tension with other values prevalent in society. However, in more recent years, a more culturally compatible image of individual success has been adopted. These changes have led to emphasis on techniques rather than shared purposes, & on self-interest rather than mutual responsibilities. Drawing on a developmental perspective, it is argued that reclaiming the spiritual heritage of the profession can provide the foundation needed to affirm values that transcend the individual & to sustain meaningful roles as catalysts for a moral community. 32 References. HA

Response to the Catholic Bishops' Letter on the U.S. Economy

Author: Hoff, Marie D11 School Social Service Saint Louis U, MO 63103

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61467531?accountid=14667

Abstract: In 1986, the US Catholic bishops issued a pastoral letter, Economic Justice for All: Catholic Social Teaching on the U.S. Economy. Reported here is a research project that evaluated the impact of the pastoral letter using a mail survey & personal interviews (N = 148 & 18 respondents, respectively). It was found that exposure to Catholic social thought (including this pastoral), a religious commitment to action for justice, & a sense of religious meaning to one's daily work were significantly associated with attitudes toward social & economic issues discussed in the letter. Implications include the need for: outreach to church communities on social justice education & action; new research on participatory justice; & expanded attention to the role of work in individual development & in community life. 4 Tables, 28 References. Modified HA

Three Books on Social Security: A Complex Portrayal

Author: Weber, George H11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61548052?accountid=14667

Abstract: A review essay on books by: Eric R. Kingson, Barbara A. Hirshorn, & John M. Cornman, Ties That Bind: The Interdependence of Generations (Washington, DC/Cabin John, Md: Seven Locks Press, 1986); Phillip Longman, Born to Pay: The New Politics of Aging in America (Boston, Mass: Houghton Mifflin, 1987); & Merton C. Bernstein & Joan Brodshaug Bernstein, Social Security: The System That Works (New York: Basic Books, 1988 [see listings in IRPSPPD No. 20]). In Ties That Bind, the social security system is presented as justified & well-suited for a US population characterized as interdependent, inseparable, & mutually supporting. Arguments about the inequity of the system are portrayed as illogical, divisive, distracting, & failing to account for economic growth & the contributions of women & immigrants to the fund. In Born To Pay, the position is taken that demographics, coupled with cultural values that encourage allocation of resources to the old & to the neglect of middle class retirement needs will result in baby boomers not receiving their full social security benefits. Several solutions to the solvency problem of the social security system are presented. In Social Security, the social security system is presented as effective in assisting the elderly in their retirement, financially solvent well into the next century, nonexploitive, & helpful in reducing the federal budget deficit. Expansion of social security coverage & the special tax break for the elderly are discussed as ways to support the system. The financial difficulties of the Medicare system are presented as being of more pressing concern, & solutions for improvement are suggested. D. Generoli

Life's Changes: A Life Cycle Perspective on Women's Economic Status

Author: Pearce, Diana M1; Moritz, Nadia1 Women & Poverty Project Instit Women's Policy Research, 1400 20th St NW Washington DC 20036

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60968215?accountid=14667

Abstract: The economic issues affecting women are determined by three main factors: economic responsibility for parenting, experience in the workforce, & marital status. A Respect Life Ethic: Women's Experience and the American Context

Author: Keightley, Georgia Masters11 Trinity Coll, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60985686?accountid=14667

Abstract: In response to Lisa Sowle Cahill ("Women, 'Respect for Life' and the Church in the United States," Social Thought, 1987, 13, 2-3, 74-86), the contribution of US women to the Roman Catholic concept of "respect for life" is considered. The meaning of the concept is discussed in the context of Christian scripture & Church teaching, as well as from the perspective of feminist theology. Women's experience is seen as a rich resource, helping to create a praxis providing witness to Catholic reverence & respect for human life. 23 References. F. S. J. Ledgister

The Need for a Land Ownership Policy

Author: McRaith, John J

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61573730?accountid=14667

Abstract: US farm policy of the 1950s & 1960s reduced the number of farmers from 5.6 million to 2.1 million. Its primary consideration was to insure that consumers could buy food cheaply; however, the policy had hidden costs, with farmers receiving an ever decreasing proportion of consumers' food dollars. Minority farmers have been especially hard hit. It is argued that the excessive tendency to selfishness within capitalism can be restrained by cooperation of government & religious institutions, & that they should work together for legislation that promotes family farming, allows enough production to feed the poor, & eliminates the economic costs of environmental conservation. 21 References. A. Waters

Catholic Charities and Pluralism: Some Problems, Trends and Opportunities

Author: Ahmann, Mathew

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61599378?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of pluralism in the human services delivery system, which is being increasingly dominated by profit-making corporations, focusing on implications for Catholic Charities agencies. Challenges to Catholic Charities' advocacy rights are assessed, & democratic process issues that impinge on Catholic Charities are examined. Unusual pressures that have been brought to bear on the nonprofit community as a whole over the past decade, as well as economic stress due to political changes in federal budget priorities, are discussed. The need for vigorous participation by Catholic Charities is stressed as essential in meeting these challenges. F. Rasmussen

The Development of Policy for the Homeless: The Role of Research

Author: Hudson, Christopher G11 School Social Work Salem State Coll, Marblehead MA 01970

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61581330?accountid=14667

Abstract: The relationship between research & policy development regarding the homelessness problem in the US is examined. After describing how homelessness came to be placed on the public policy agenda, it is argued that policy development has been thwarted by the ability of key participants to use research to the advantage of their own political position. A review of studies published between 1979 & 1984 reveals that research has been focused on counting & describing the homeless, supporting policy in the emergent stage; but through failing to confront the fundamental economic, political, demographic, & structural problems that underlie homelessness, it has inhibited policy legitimation & mobilization. A case study of policy development in Chicago & other major areas of Ill reveals the minor role played by research. It is argued that future studies must develop a broader perspective so as not to perpetuate the notion that homelessness is an individual problem that does not require full-fledged government interventions. Suggestions are offered to help social workers guide rather than rationalize current policy initiatives through redesigning research. 1 Table, 20 References. K. Hyatt

Social Work as an Holistic System of Activity

Author: Imbrogno, Salvatore1; Canda, Edward R1 Coll Social Work Ohio State U, Columbus 43210

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61579865?accountid=14667

Abstract: Recent trends in paradigm building within the social welfare field advocate for an approach that is holistic, systemic, phenomenological, & nondichotomous. Here, a contribution to such an approach is offered by converging key ideas from general system theory & Oriental philosophy, in particular, the Chinese Book of Changes, or I Ching, the most important ancient codification of basic philosophical principles of Chinese civilization. General system theory, which has long influenced social welfare's efforts in holistic thinking, offers a fitting point of connection between Oriental philosophy & social work paradigm building. These ideas provide a basis for a model of social welfare as a holistic system of professional activity. This approach helps to overcome dichotomies in social welfare concepts & practice, & also provides a common ground of understanding between Eastern & Western views of professional practices. 1 Figure, 44 References. AA

Conceptualizing Spirituality for Social Work: Insights from Diverse Perspectives

Author: Canda, Edward R11 School Social Work U Iowa, Iowa City 52242

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61579981?accountid=14667

Abstract: A conceptualization of spirituality for social work that has interreligious & transcultural applicability is proposed, based on a review of the literature, & interviews conducted with 18 social work scholars who have published or presented at national conferences on this topic. Spirituality is conceptualized as the gestalt of the process of human life & development, the central dynamic of which is the person's search for a sense of meaning & purpose through relationships between self, other people, the nonhuman environment, & ultimate reality (as described in theistic, nontheistic, or atheistic terms). The conceptualization incorporates insights from the atheist, Buddhist, Christian, existentialist, Jewish, & shamanistic perspectives. As spirituality is a fundamental aspect of human experience, it has significance for all areas of social work. General suggestions & implications for innovation within theory, values, practice, education, & research are offered for the development of spiritually sensitive social work. 1 Table, 1 Figure, 54 References. Modified AA

The Challenge and Promise in Rural Development

Author: Gratto, Stephen H11 Catholic Charities, PO Box 296 Ogdensburg NY 13669

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61546503?accountid=14667

Abstract: Promotion of community development, especially by partnerships involving government, social agencies -- including Catholic organizations -- & local communities, is argued to be the only way to alleviate the continuing social & economic crisis in the rural US. Humanistic Alternatives to the Limits of Scientific Knowledge: The Case of Ethical Dilemmas in Social Work Practice

Author: Goldstein, Howard11 School Applied Social Services Case Western U, Cleveland OH 44106

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61473327?accountid=14667

Abstract: Many of the problems expressed by clients in social work & psychotherapy represent ethical dilemmas that are indicative of the search for solutions when choices must be made but no comfortable answers are apparent, & where conflicting demands & outcomes are inevitable. In large part, standard education for practice rooted in scientific methods or prescriptive theories offers the practitioner little in terms of preparation for dealing with these dilemmas. The tendency, therefore, is to "psychologize" or objectify the dilemma, or otherwise treat it in utilitarian terms. Here, a narrative approach to practice is proposed that enables the practitioner to enter into & begin to make sense of the stories & themes that illuminate the client's life & character. In this way, the practitioner joins with the client in the search for solutions in accord with the client's way of thinking, culture & community, valued principles of living, & spiritual beliefs. The foundations for this approach lie in the humanities & include contributions from: literature, philosophy, history, & religion; an identified body of humanistic literature in social work; & the client's own story. 28 References. AA

Religious Self-Disclosure in Christian Family Service Agencies

Author: Boynton, Gerald W11 Graduate School Social Work U Houston University Park, TX 77004

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61571102?accountid=14667

Abstract: There has been concern over whether social workers in sectarian settings are able to refrain from imposing their own or agencies' religious values on their clients, a violation of professional norms. Religious self-disclosure among 73 therapists in 25 Church of Christ family agencies located in the southeastern & southwestern US is investigated, comparing a subsample of 29 MSWs to the larger sample. A survey instrument was designed to collect data on therapists' demographic variables & their degree of self-disclosure concerning their values/beliefs/experiences regarding childrearing, marriage, sex, & religion. Results indicate that both the MSWs & larger sample are low self-disclosers, tending instead to employ the more traditional therapeutic techniques used by their counterparts in secular settings. Suggestions are provided for exploring the use of religious self-disclosure in other sectarian therapeutic situations. 5 Tables, 29 References. K. Hyatt

Beyond Empiricism: Toward a Holistic Conception of Social Work

Author: Weick, Ann11 School Social Welfare U Kansas, Lawrence 66045

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61437944?accountid=14667

Abstract: The assumptions of classical science have deeply influenced the knowledge-building activities of the profession, even though the physical sciences have developed far beyond the strict empiricism embodied in Newtonian physics. By using the more contemporary assumptions of quantum theory, it is possible for new meaning to be brought to traditional social work concepts. The resemblances between medieval & quantum thought are considered as a way of bringing a clearer understanding to the concept of person-in-environment. The underlying holistic perspective is seen as a more compatible premise for social work than the fragmented, mechanistic approach of classical science. 23 References. AA

The Unemployed and the Poor: Differing Perceptions of Their Needs in a Community

Author: Brabson, Howard V1; Himle, David P1 School Social Work U Michigan, Ann Arbor 48109-1285

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61011431?accountid=14667

Abstract: A report on a study of semi-Ru midwestern county that examined the nature of social problems, availability of services, & barriers to service utilization in the community, as perceived by the poor, the unemployed, & community leaders. Interview data obtained from 470 poor & unemployed Rs & 108 key informants (community leaders) showed that those who were responsible for planning social services for the unemployed & the poor had different perceptions of problems & social service needs than the poor & unemployed themselves, & were unaware of the perception gap between the two groups. The findings also indicated that people turned to their churches to receive social services, information, & referrals. It is concluded that there is a need for greater involvement of both the unemployed & poor & community leaders in the planning processes of the community, & a greater need for supporting the role of churches as a part of the social welfare delivery system. 5 Tables, 3 Illustrations, 14 References. Modified AA

Contribution of Religious Values to Social Work and the Law

Author: Siporin, Max11 School Social Welfare State U New York, Albany 12222

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60914358?accountid=14667

Abstract: Religious values were greatly influential in the development of the social work & legal professions. Increasingly, the secularization of social work & the law has led to major discrepancies between their professional value systems & religious values. Differences between these value systems are identified & their essential moral nature is clarified. The common societal functions of these institutions help to foster social cooperation & to deal with deviant behavior & dependency. It is suggested that religious values can be applied to help renew the value systems of the social work & legal professions & to meet needs for their greater effectiveness. 79 References. AA

Meeting Human Needs: The Role of Government

Author: Weber, Leonard J11 Mercy Coll, Detroit MI 48219

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61554517?accountid=14667

Abstract: Three major views of the role of government in meeting the needs of the disadvantaged have been widely held in the US. In the traditional view, government exists only to protect individual rights, & the needs of the poor are to be met through the market system & through individual self-interest. In the humanitarian view, government exists to regulate the free-market system & to confer remedial benefits on the disadvantaged. In the communitarian view, only now emerging, government exists to serve the goal of fraternity, & private property should be subordinated to common use. These ideas have consequences for the future shape of US policy. 4 References. W. H. Stoddard

Religion, Research, and Social Work

Author: Faver, Catherine A11 Coll Social Work U Tennessee, Knoxville 37996

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61581565?accountid=14667

Abstract: If taken seriously, insights & perspectives from the great religious traditions can expand & enrich social work's approach to knowledge development. Specifically, religious theology has implications for social work research in three areas: (1) insights from religion can affect the questions addressed in social work research by highlighting neglected topics & complex problems requiring study; (2) perspectives from religion can affect social work's methods of inquiry by encouraging consideration of multiple types & sources of knowledge & by compelling researchers to seek knowledge from people in diverse social locations; & (3) attention to religion can affect the interpretation of findings in social work research by challenging commonly accepted notions of objectivity & by encouraging full consideration of alternative explanations of reality & understanding of truth. 2 Illustrations, 28 References. Modified AA

Residual or Prophetic? The Cultural Fate of Roman Catholic Sexual Ethics of Abortion and Contraception

Author: Kelly, James R11 Fordham U, Bronx NY 10458

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60977200?accountid=14667

Abstract: A review of findings on the contraception & abortion attitudes & practices of Catholics & others, with focus on Catholic sexual ethics. The data show widespread dissent among Catholics from official teaching, although Catholic practice & opinion remain distinguishable from mainstream US opinion & practice. There are several reasons for anticipating that these differences will persist: disagreement with Church doctrine has not resulted in widespread disaffiliation; natural family planning methods are officially promoted & have received some medical & feminist endorsement; & Catholic social thought now links issues of sexuality & social justice, making it less plausible to characterize Catholic sexual ethics as morally repressive & arbitrary. 42 References. The Introduction of the Social Sciences in the Catholic University of America 1895-1909

Author: Nuesse, C Joseph11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60960503?accountid=14667

Abstract: The Catholic U of America, chartered in 1887, became the principal channel through which the modern U movement was introduced into US Catholic higher education. It was pioneering when, in 1895, it included economics, politics, & sociology in its first curriculum in the arts & sciences, which were still being offered only at the graduate level. Both theoretical & practical concerns were manifest from the beginning. Though a department of politics could not be organized for many years, the first professors of economics & sociology shared an interest in the contemporary labor movement. William J. Kerby, an Iowa priest who had been sent to Louvain for his doctorate, became the founding chairman of the department of sociology, through which he undertook to begin the professionalization of social work under Catholic auspices. 48 References. AA

The "Catholic Ethic" vs the "Protestant Ethic": Catholic Social Service and the Welfare State

Author: Tropman, John E11 School Social Work U Michigan, Ann Arbor 48109

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61619176?accountid=14667

Abstract: The concept of the "Catholic ethic" is introduced as a competing value system to that embodied in the "Protestant ethic," as developed by Max Weber. Features of the Catholic ethic include: (1) ambivalence concerning wealth; (2) an instrumental attitude toward work; (3) support of the family (as opposed to personal achievement); (4) a tradition of charity; (5) a tradition of bureaucracy; & (6) fault forgiveness. It is argued that such an ethic is supportive of welfare state activities, social policies, & practices, in contrast to the negative orientation of the Protestant ethic toward the welfare state. Empirical evidence for the Catholic orientation is presented, & it is suggested that further research explore other "ethics" (eg, a Jewish ethic or a Muslim ethic) & their relationship to social welfare. 47 References. Modified AA

Racism: White Problem, White Disadvantage

Author: Morrison, John D11 School Social Work U Pennsylvania, Philadelphia 19104

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61477343?accountid=14667

Abstract: White efforts to reduce racism in the US are diminished by the assumption that racism's negative effects are experienced by blacks alone. Given a definition of racism in terms of the subordination of one part of a population by another, it is evident that racism is characteristically a white behavior pattern. Racism can exist both on the individual level, in such forms as prejudice, discrimination, conformity, & inaction, & on the institutional level. Racism limits the power of white organizations, damages the economic position of whites, creates social problems that affect whites as well as blacks, limits housing choices for whites, cuts support for social programs, & leads to racist behavior by social agencies. These impose costs on whites that could be removed through collective social action, training for nonracist practice, support for black organization, service in black-related organizations, support for integrated situations, & individual action. 33 References. W. H. Stoddard

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Racism%3A+White+Problem%2C+White+Disadvantage&amp;rft.au=Morrison%2C+John+D&amp;rft.aulast=Morrison&amp;rft.aufirst=John&amp;rft.date=1986-01-01&amp;rft.volume=12&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=31&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Deviance, Morality and Social Work Therapy

Author: Siporin, Max11 State U New York, Albany 12222

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61614838?accountid=14667

Abstract: Conceptions of normal/abnormal behavior, deviance, mental disorder, & psychopathology are discussed & related to issues about morality/immorality. It is argued that the present libertarian & relativistic moral philosophy & mental health ethic held by social workers undermine their commitment to both cultural pluralism & social integration/cohesion. Confusion about mental health & disorder impairs the ability of the social work profession to meet the needs of clients or society for moral guidance in solving problems in social living. Moral/ethical & communal aspects of the helping process are identified, & implications provided for social work practice. 84 References. Modified HA

Traditional Values about Family Behavior: The Case of the Chicano Client

Author: Galan, Fernando Javier11 Graduate School Social Work U Houston, University Park TX 77004

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61473756?accountid=14667

Abstract: Chicanos requesting assistance from Catholic social agencies are viewed from a perspective of traditional family values & behavior. This leads to a better understanding of the client's worldview, & of how the client's value system & beliefs influence his/her definition & perception of the problem, as well as what might best resolve it. Five values that form the core of a Chicano client's worldview are explored: (1) nobleza, the inherent knowledge of peace & harmony; (2) honor, or the expression of decent behavior, which will reflect well on the family; (3) respecto, a regard for the feelings of others as well as the maintenance of formal family relationships; (4) verguenza, which connotes the shame "of having exposed the family to disgrace"; & (5) lastima, the familial response to the expression of a member's verguenza. Understanding these principles helps Catholic social workers to incorporate culturally prescribed behaviors into the treatment plan. 12 References. R. McCarthy

The Dynamics of Hispanic Populations: A Description and Comparison

Author: Estrada, Leobardo F11 Graduate School Architecture & Urban Planning U California, Los Angeles 90024

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60960383?accountid=14667

Abstract: Between 1970 & 1980, the Hispanic population of the US grew dramatically, as revealed by census data. This trend can be explained on the basis of the population's youthful age structure & of continued legal & illegal immigration. The majority reside in Calif, Tex, & NY; by region, the southwest, NY/NJ, Fla, & Ill have high Hispanic populations. Hispanics are highly urbanized, second only to Asians; & Spanish is the second most widely used language in the US. SE characteristics of this population are briefly reviewed & compared with those of other ethnic groups. It is important to recognize distinctions within the Hispanic population, especially between ethnic subgroups. 7 Tables, 2 Graphs. W. H. Stoddard

Comparison between the Perceptions of Human Service Workers and Chicano Clients

Author: Gomez, Ernesto1; Becker, Roy E1 Worden School Social Service Our Lady Lake U, San Antonio TX 78285

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61603085?accountid=14667

Abstract: The agreement between human service workers' & Chicano clients' perceptions concerning initial assessments & changes in problem severity is examined based on data from a larger study that evaluated the effectiveness of casework services with Chicano clients. Direct service workers (N = 28) & Chicano clients (N = 87) of 2 community mental health centers in southern Tex completed a questionnaire both before & after casework services. Findings show that worker/client perceptions of severity are incongruent both in initial assessment & in regard to severity change. Involvement of Chicano clients in the assessment process is suggested as a means to increase communication & agreement in treatment perceptions. 3 Tables, 16 References. R. McCarthy

The Case for a Non-Economic Definition of Poverty

Author: Marciniak, Ed11 Instit Urban Life, 14 E Chestnut St Chicago IL 60611

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60971667?accountid=14667

Abstract: While poverty has been defined primarily in economic terms in the US since the Great Depression, such a definition fails to capture the essence of poverty. Three noneconomic categories of poverty are distinguished: mainstream poverty, characteristic of families experiencing temporary difficulties; case poverty, characteristic of those with special permanent handicaps; & social poverty, characteristic of those existing in social conditions that limit their lives & the lives of all those around them. Social poverty, particularly, has grown in recent years. Reducing its extent requires efforts to revitalize the neighborhood support system, reduce alienation, & reduce dependency on government. W. H. Stoddard

Medicare: Ethical Issues in Public Policy for the Elderly

Author: Collopy, Bartholomew J11 Third Age Center Fordham U, Bronx NY 10458

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61606654?accountid=14667

Abstract: Highly publicized budgetary "scares" have effectively fiscalized most recent discussion of the Medicare program. As a result, Medicare's ethical ambiguities, long curtained behind political strategies, have been further removed from scrutiny. Ethical analysis reveals, however, that Medicare is deeply conflicted in terms of distributive justice. The program suffers from structural biases tied to: (1) age-based membership; (2) aggregate identification of elderly financial/medical need; & (3) meritarian descriptions of eligibility & coverage. The age-based membership encourages negative stereotypes, prevents carefully targeted response to health & economic need, extends assistance to the self-sufficient, & sows cynicism about all social programs for the elderly. Medicare's original aggregate justifications have proved to be highly time-bound & expensive, increasingly inaccurate, & inefficient; currently suggested aggregate "solutions" threaten to intensify inequity & inefficiency. Finally, in addressing elderly need through the mechanisms of merit, Medicare has ideologically blurred crucial ethical distinctions. In practice, this ideological blur has allowed meritarian biases to undercut, often to nullify, adequate medical care for the elderly. 9 References. AA

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Medicare%3A+Ethical+Issues+in+Public+Policy+for+the+Elderly&amp;rft.au=Collopy%2C+Bartholomew+J&amp;rft.aulast=Collopy&amp;rft.aufirst=Bartholomew&amp;rft.date=1985-04-01&amp;rft.volume=11&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=5&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

The Aging, Income Support Programs, and Economic Well-Being: A Catholic Perspective

Author: Ryle, Edward J11 Arizona Catholic Conference, Phoenix

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61558274?accountid=14667

Abstract: The economic situation of the aging is discussed from the point of view of Catholic social thought as expressed in the social encyclicals, documents of Vatican II, etc. The US may be facing a serious budgetary crisis, which will necessitate hard choices about health & income support programs. The basic sustenance needs of the poor must take precedence over lesser needs & rights of the Mc & Uc. Reductions in military spending, revising the tax reductions of the Economic Recovery Tax Act of 1981, & increasing employment can enable continuing support of the elderly. 3 Tables, 24 References. S. McAneny

A Sociological Analysis and Theological Reflection on Adoption Services in Catholic Charities Agencies

Author: Voss, Richard11 Chester County Office Catholic Social Services, Philadelphia PA

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61055752?accountid=14667

Abstract: The gradual decline in adoption is discussed, & the reasons why pregnant teenagers choose abortion or single parenthood are examined. Procedures followed by adoption agencies frequently show little concern for the unwed mother's feelings; she is often subjected to heartless badgering, forced to sign forms that use terms like "illegitimate child" & "termination of parental rights," & treated like a criminal. Adoption services must be made more accessible, affordable, & sensitive to the dignity & privacy of their clients. 18 References. S. McAneny

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61439325?accountid=14667

Refugee Women in a Vertical Village: Lowland Laotians in St. Louis

Author: Rynearson, Ann M; DeVoe, Pamela A

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/60967648?accountid=14667

Abstract: Southeast Asian refugees in the US differ from most previous immigrant groups in including a high proportion of women. The role of women in their community structures is examined through a case study of an apartment building in central St. Louis, Mo, whose occupants included 122 lowland Laotians occupying 32 of the 96 apartments in the building. The residents are involved in an elaborate mutual aid system resembling those existing in their homeland. Food exchange is an important part of this system. Many tasks are performed by both sexes, including child care, & this flexibility helps families adapt to difficult work schedules. Both men & women work, reflecting traditional customs that encourage women's economic activities. Women have significant roles to play in many ceremonies; in particular, they prepare the foods consumed during many such ceremonies. It is concluded that the presence of women is crucial to community functioning. 34 References. W. H. Stoddard

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocabsshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Refugee+Women+in+a+Vertical+Village%3A+Lowland+Laotians+in+St.+Louis&amp;rft.au=Rynearson%2C+Ann+M%3BDeVoe%2C+Pamela+A&amp;rft.aulast=Rynearson&amp;rft.aufirst=Ann&amp;rft.date=1984-07-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=33&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Self-Help/Mutual Aid in Changing Communities

Author: Borman, Leonard D11 Self-Help Center, Evanston IL 60204-9998

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61567457?accountid=14667

Abstract: The development of self-help/mutual-aid groups represents an adaptive strategy of significant benefit to refugees being resettled in the US. Common characteristics of such groups are identified: membership based on mutual recognition; governance through self-regulation; emphasis on self-reliance & group affiliation; distinctive belief systems & ideologies; & the impact of the larger group context. Problems of Kalmuk Mongol refugees, described on the basis of personal experience with this group, illustrate some of these issues. Implications for the strategies pursued by officials seeking to help refugee populations are drawn. 13 References. W. H. Stoddard

Toward a Moral Philosophy for Social Work: 1983 O'Grady Award Winner

Author: Hughes, John J11 George Mason U, Fairfax VA 22030

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61620918?accountid=14667

Abstract: The characteristics of the ideal moral foundation for social policy & ethics are delineated, emphasizing the concept of natural law. Objectivity, universality, flexibility, & rationality are some of the criteria proposed for a moral philosophy. Some optional philosophies include subjectivism, positivism, utilitarianism, & natural law, which is cited as the oldest moral doctrine. John Courtney Murray's definition of natural law is discussed (We Hold These Truths: Catholic Reflections on the American Proposition, New York: Sheed & Ward, 1960, 327-328). Although international social work codes contain references to natural law (as humanitarianism), schools have been remiss in teaching the morals underlying social work. Catholic schools are cited as the exceptions. Since the development & maintenance of moral character are seen as the primary function of social work, this aspect necessitates more attention. 23 References. D. Graves.

Competence Clarification in Social Work Practice

Author: Maluccio, Anthony N1; Libassi, Mary Frances1 School Social Work U Connecticut, West Hartford 06117

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61552691?accountid=14667

Abstract: Social workers have long stressed the importance of the person-environment configuration in the functioning & development of human beings. In particular, in recent years various approaches to social work practice have emphasized ways of helping clients to develop their potentialities & coping skills by identifying & mobilizing actual or latent resources in themselves & their environments. In this regard, the concept of competence clarification is proposed -- the process of identifying & understanding one's competence in coping with environmental challenges. Competence clarification is viewed as an integral component of assessment. Its purposes are to: (1) clarify the competence of the client system; (2) identify the characteristics of the environment that influence a client's coping & adaptive patterns; & (3) evaluate the goodness of fit between the client system & its impinging environment. 7 References. Modified AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Competence+Clarification+in+Social+Work+Practice&amp;rft.au=Maluccio%2C+Anthony+N%3BLibassi%2C+Mary+Frances&amp;rft.aulast=Maluccio&amp;rft.aufirst=Anthony&amp;rft.date=1984-04-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=51&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Towards Confidence: Catholic Social Thought in North America

Author: Kelly, James R11 Fordham U, Bronx NY 10458

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61031090?accountid=14667

Abstract: US Catholic social thought has always taught that the economic order ought not to be thought of as autonomous but subordinate to the moral order & the achievement of the common good. An empirical survey, (Wilson, John, Religion in American Society, Prentice-Hall, 1978) shows that, for the most part, Catholic voting behavior & economic attitudes have reflected this teaching. Catholic social thought tries to keep alive in a principled way, with deep community roots, some assumptions indispensable for any humane economic order: economic rationality ought not be the final criteria of rational appraisal of the economy; the community through the state has obligations in justice to help the poor; all help should respect the dignity of the recipients; no government policy is "neutral" & the basic needs of the poor warrant more consideration than the luxuries of the rich. But while Catholic intellectuals are now less likely than before to find US liberal pragmatism superior to the Catholic social tradition, it remains true that this tradition of social thought will not easily fit any of the dominant modes of political thought, which is both an advantage & a disadvantage. 23 References. AA

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocabsshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Towards+Confidence%3A+Catholic+Social+Thought+in+North+America&amp;rft.au=Kelly%2C+James+R&amp;rft.aulast=Kelly&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rft.date=1984-04-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=59&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

A National Housing Vision: We Need More Than a Dream

Author: Harvey, Thomas J11 National Conference Catholic Charities, 1346 Connecticut Ave NW Suite 307 Washington DC 20036

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61582557?accountid=14667

Abstract: In its social teaching, the Catholic Church stresses that human dignity, not work or wealth, is the ultimate rationale for meeting needs, including the need for decent housing. From the earliest days in the US, it has had a particular concern for the poor & the elderly & has offered various forms of residential & nursing care. Parishes are now extending their efforts to establish creative life-support centers & professional Catholic agencies are offering health & home care. The Church has been a partner with the profit sector in land use & in organizational leadership in sponsoring better housing for the elderly with subsidized rents to assure access for the poor. It recognizes that if its social teaching is to be implemented, there must be analysis & planning before there is action, & that shared responsibility & cooperation with other groups are needed if housing problems are to be solved. 7 References. AA.

Housing Needs of the Elderly and How to Meet Them

Author: Dolbeare, Cushing

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61620257?accountid=14667

Abstract: An assessment is presented of the housing needs of the elderly, in the context of those of low-income groups in the US, focusing on housing policies of the Reagan administration, & based on 1980/81 data from the Annual Housing Survey of the US Dept of Housing & Ur Development. Statistics show that about 6 million renter households must pay more than 50% of their income for rent, that minorities are disproportionately represented among low-income renter households, & that the demand for low-cost housing units greatly exceeds the supply. Programs for federal subsidies for low-income groups' housing needs have been sharply reduced under the present administration, while federal support for middle- & upper-income level households' housing needs remains about the same. Some components in a low-income housing program being developed by the National Low Income Housing Coalition are presented, emphasizing fair housing legislation, income-based housing entitlement programs, reduction of subsidies to Mc & Uc groups, & development of adequate credit & financing policies. 3 Tables, 5 References. D. Dunseath.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Housing+Needs+of+the+Elderly+and+How+to+Meet+Them&amp;rft.au=Dolbeare%2C+Cushing&amp;rft.aulast=Dolbeare&amp;rft.aufirst=Cushing&amp;rft.date=1984-01-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=16&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Residents in Shared Housing

Author: Schreter, Carol

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61597959?accountid=14667

Abstract: Aspects & assumptions about shared housing are examined, in the light of renewed attention to the advantages of shared housing paid by federal policymakers, gerontologists, & others. Types of shared housing are considered in the categories of self-initiated, agency-assisted, & agency-sponsored. While shared housing is most commonly thought of in terms of its financial & practical advantages for frail elderly, it has numerous advantages for all age groups. Data from 1981/82 interviews with housesharers in the Washington, DC, area (N = 79) reveal some characteristics & preferences. While pooling financial resources was an obvious motivation for most sharers, many homesharers had had severe health setbacks & valued housemates, especially nonrelated ones, for reasons of security. The notion that shared housing is age-segregated is refuted, & the values of intergenerational housing arranged by an agency matching program are described. The importance of matching congenial personalities regardless of differences in age is emphasized. 14 References. D. Dunseath.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Residents+in+Shared+Housing&amp;rft.au=Schreter%2C+Carol&amp;rft.aulast=Schreter&amp;rft.aufirst=Carol&amp;rft.date=1984-01-01&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=30&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Enhancing Housing Environments for the Elderly: The Role of Staff

Author: Creedon, Michael A

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61567481?accountid=14667

Abstract: Presented in the context of improving elderly housing situations are considerations for staff & housing personnel. Attempts should be made where possible to compensate for the loss of personal effects & the loss of the decision-making role. Priority is placed on the following: (1) familiarizing elderly with housing facilities before they become residents; (2) roommate or house-mate compatibility; (3) providing adequate space for personal privacy; (4) health, medication, & nutrition concerns; & (5) development of therapeutic opportunities for communication & expression among housing-group members. 16 References. D. Dunseath.

Morality and Immorality in Working with Clients

Author: Siporin, Max11 School Social Welfare Rockefeller Coll Public Affairs State U New York, Albany 12222

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61582518?accountid=14667

Abstract: The avoidance of moral/ethical difficulties by clients & social workers, & the social worker's lack of knowledge & skill in how to deal with these problems is dysfunctional for both clients & social workers. The nature & effects of this state of affairs are identified, with a critical examination of the libertarian, relativistic moral orientation that is prevalent among social workers. Conceptual distinctions are clarified & suggestions made for more effective helping processes in regard to moral/ethical decisions & actions. 43 References. AA.

Values, Religion, and Social Work Practice

Author: Constable, Robert T11 Jane Addams School Social Work U Illinois, Chicago 60680

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61616203?accountid=14667

Abstract: A rationale for values in social work is developed based on conceptions of individual worth & dignity & the reciprocal obligations of individuals & society. Out of these grow the general goals of social work professional activity: freedom, justice, & relational love or "caritas." Four core practice values are explicated together with twenty-six ethical practice principles. The relation of professional values & ethical practice principles to ideologies & religion is discussed. 33 References. AA.

Ammending the Constitution to Accomplish Social Goals

Author: Fox, William F, Jr11 School Law Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61623336?accountid=14667

Abstract: The history of US constitutional amendments is briefly reviewed. Discussed is the failure to distinguish between the wisdom of the amendment process & that of particular amendments. Factors to be considered when evaluating an amendment are outlined: language, possible enforcement problems, need for a national consensus, & effects on other parts of the Constitution. It is argued that, when considering amendments enforcing a specific social or economic policy, history must be kept in mind: many issues raised by ratification of an amendment must be resolved in court. Only two amendments enforcing a social policy (prohibition & the abolition of slavery) have been ratified. 8 References. I. Kocher.

Market Oriented Health Policy: An Analysis of the Pro-Competition Strategy

Author: Kenney, Jay11 Washington Hospital Center, 110 Irving NW Washington DC 20010

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61440860?accountid=14667

Abstract: The problem of increasing health care costs is outlined with reference to statistical data from 1979. Discussed are four basic elements of proposed procompetition health plans (multiple choice, fixed-dollar subsidy, application of the same rules to all qualified health plans, MDs as competing economic units), attempts to eliminate "perversive incentives" that produce overinsurance & overutilization by modifying employment-based tax incentives, & the proposal to "cash out" Medicare & Medicaid by switching to a voucher system. Negative reactions to the proposals by various interest groups & potential problems of adverse selection, cost shifting, & vouchers are reviewed. 3 Figures, 13 References. I. Kocher.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Market+Oriented+Health+Policy%3A+An+Analysis+of+the+Pro-Competition+Strategy&amp;rft.au=Kenney%2C+Jay&amp;rft.aulast=Kenney&amp;rft.aufirst=Jay&amp;rft.date=1983-07-01&amp;rft.volume=9&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=15&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Understanding Value Deficiencies in Delinquent Behavior

Author: Saari, Carolyn11 School Social Work Loyola U, Chicago IL 60611

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61047294?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of psychoanalytic assumptions that have influenced social work, & theories that suggest: (1) that affective experience develops as part of general conceptual development, (2) that children without highly differentiated affective experiences will fail to develop the expected value system & will tend not to see possibilities in the inner & nonmaterial aspects of lifestyles, & (3) that the forced reliance on immediate, poorly planned actions will result in delinquency. The case history of a delinquent girl is presented & a reformulation of traditional theory proposed: the failure to develop coping structures leads to prolonged dependency (instead of failure to cope being caused by dependency needs). It is argued that viewing values as conceptualized affects may help in appreciating the usefulness of values to people in planning & understanding their own actions & in preparing for full participation in society. It is concluded that, if it is true that normal development proceeds from action through fantasy to mature conceptual ability, social workers must encourage youths to follow that path. 34 References. I. Kocher

Great and Small Traditions in Chilean Social Work

Author: Jimenez de Barros, Monica11 School Social Work Pontifical Catholic U, Santiago Chile

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61552721?accountid=14667

Abstract: A description of "great" & "small" traditions in Chilean social work. The former include: its mission & values; objects of action; & basic objectives that orient social work practice toward its primary aims. The latter include: specific objectives & daily activities; types of services or units of intervention; methodologies used; & the overall orientation of social workers toward social problems. Also described are sociostructural mechanisms for developing & transmitting the traditions of Chilean social work through diverse schools, the Assoc of Social Workers, & the Journal of Social Work of the Catholic U of Chile. 7 References. AA.

Organized Social Work and the Welfare State

Author: Hughes, John J11 George Mason U, Fairfax VA 22030

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61584409?accountid=14667

Abstract: In the context of current misgivings about the welfare state, the policy positions of the organized US social work profession are examined, critically exploring the profession's value congruence with that of the larger society, aspects of its rationality in policy development, & its attention to issues of political & economic feasibility. Finding the profession deficient on all three dimensions, suggestions are offered for future policy directions. 10 References. AA.

Catholic Social Service and Transcendental Values

Author: Caplis, Regina

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61589611?accountid=14667

Abstract: The uniqueness & strength of Catholic social services lie in the role accorded to religious values, but Catholic therapists & counselors have yet to fully integrate their religious beliefs into professional services offered by organizations such as the Catholic Charities & Catholic Social Service. To fulfill their goals, the professionalism, advanced study, & specialization of social service workers in these organizations must be liberated from the clinical pragmatism & humanistic idealism that dominate the mental health profession as a whole; the scientific method, although important, is no substitute for spiritual values. The benefits of "prayer therapy" should be researched by the National Catholic School of Social Service, & the relationship between "transcendental values" & good mental health studied. 39 References. J. Weber.

Preparation for Marriage: Promise and Problems

Author: Mullaney, Joan Ward1; Otey, Emeline1 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61559042?accountid=14667

Abstract: Data from 323 participants (N = 85 spouses, 156 priests, 82 parents) in the Catholic Young Married Program (YMP) in Albany, NY -- a preparation program for marrying couples with at least one partner under 21, focusing on responsibilities of marriage, relationship issues, spiritual life, sexuality, parenthood, etc -- were analyzed to measure the program's effectiveness. Components of the YMP include meetings of the engaged couple with priests, counselors, & married couples; couple-to-couple meetings were found to be the most beneficial in preparing for the day-to-day pressures of marriage. The value of the YMP as a method of predicting marital happiness & assessing a couple's readiness for marriage is stressed; a correlation is noted between number of YMP programs participated in & degree of expressed marital satisfaction. Overall findings suggest that preparation should place greater emphasis on "realities" of married life, especially through increased utilization of the married couple program. 4 Table, 25 References. J. Weber.

Strengthening Families: Social Policy and Related Issues

Author: Bateman, Richard W11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61623827?accountid=14667

Abstract: Problems related to the goal of strengthening family life are identified, means to resolve those problems are offered, & a framework for developing more enlightened family policy is outlined. Stressing the responsibility of the social work profession to influence social policy, a descriptive analysis is presented of the systems framework used by many sociologists & other professionals to view the family: society is a system of interrelated institutions that function to attain certain valued ends, & each institution or subsystem, eg, the family, is affected by change in any other part of the larger system. The White House Conference on Families is reviewed, within the systems framework, & it is concluded that the conference was in fact a rejection of federal leadership responsibility. Reasons for this conclusion are outlined. 11 References. Modified AA.

Social Work's Conceptual Frameworks: Uniqueness and Strategies -- The Time Is Now

Author: Meyer, Carol H11 School Social Work Columbia U, New York NY 10027

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61441033?accountid=14667

Abstract: The need for definitions of US social work & its conceptual frameworks is addressed, focusing on the model of interaction between individuals & their environment. Social workers' difficulties in promoting beneficial interactions are noted. The usual focus on either person or environment & the centrality of the assessment process in developing alternatives are stressed. Scapegoating of social workers & their clients is examined as an outcome of role ambiguities & contradictory social policies; the importance of using the transactional perspective to overcome these stigmas is discussed & illustrated. Prospects for further specialization are reviewed, emphasizing the difference between a methodological & a "domain" conception of social work. 4 References. L. Whittemore.

Knowledge Base for Clinical Social Work Practice

Author: Chescheir, Martha

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61635333?accountid=14667

Abstract: The fluid parameters of US social work practice are considered in a summary of the profession's fundamental knowledge base. Five clearly defined areas of expertise & concern are detailed: (1) work with individuals in their social context; (2) work with the family as a facilitating environment; (3) group process therapy oriented toward tasks & problem solving; (4) management work with organizations & social systems to improve general social conditions; & (5) management of situational & maturational crises. Concepts from personality theory, social systems theory, & social psychology are used in all areas; potential applications of an object relations approach are considered as well, stressing a need for connective theories concerned with the interface between individual & environment. 9 References. Modified Author Introduction.

Research and the Social Work Practitioner: An Overview

Author: Timberlake, Elizabeth M; Carr, Lewis W

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61480431?accountid=14667

Abstract: The needs & format of social work research in the US are reviewed, focusing on new professional & managerial demands. The low level of practitioner participation in current research is discussed, along with the poor fit between practice & theory; strategies for formulating research problems, designs, & methods of data collection are outlined extensively, comparing single-subject, case comparison, & historical, longitudinal, & experimental control group methods. The value for the practitioner of acquiring familiarity with research literature & techniques is discussed in terms of an enhanced knowledge base for future practice. 35 References. L. Whittemore.

Education for Doctoral Social Work Clinical Practice in the 1980s

Author: Orcutt, Ben A1; Mills, Paul R, Jr1 U Alabama, Tuscaloosa 35486

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61626713?accountid=14667

Abstract: Education for doctoral social work clinical practice in the 1980s is likely to emphasize specificity in middle-range theory; practice methodology; & the integration of theory, research, & practice. An advanced practice model is presented that integrates theory, knowledge building, & the evaluation of change in the clinical case process. Evaluation of experience with this model, as rated on a 4-point scale by 9 U of Alabama doctoral students, was positive. 4 Tables, 19 References. Modified AA.

Social Change and the Family: An Historical Perspective with Family Impact Assessment Principles for Catholic Charities

Author: Preister, Steven11 National Center Family Studies Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61605041?accountid=14667

Abstract: The family is examined in a historical context, & the changes taking place in its structure are outlined, eg, more divorce & remarriage, single-parent households, two-career families, & childless marriages. Within the Catholic Church, divorce, remarriage, invalid marriages, marriage to non-Catholics, & annulments have all increased dramatically. Two earlier forms of the family are described -- in an agricultural society, & in an industrial society. Four value conclusions are drawn that contrast the two types of families: (1) the rights & needs of families vs those of individuals; (2) the cohesion of the family vs later adaptability; (3) family-based services vs institutionalization of those services; & (4) the politicizing of the family. On this basis a framework is built for Catholic Charities to develop & expand a Catholic ministry to the family. An emphasis on parish social ministry & parish-based services is seen as crucial. It is concluded that society must develop a style of family life responsive to the needs of its members, in a parish community of Christian support. 34 References. Modified AA.

Family Secrets in Family Therapy: An Ethical Dilemma

Author: Cristy, Barbara L E11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61625316?accountid=14667

Abstract: Ethical problems in family therapy typically arise from concern with confidentiality. They may be more complicated than those of more traditional therapy because of the greater number of people involved. An example of an ethical dilemma is presented, drawn from participant observation in a psychiatric facility, & concerning family secrecy about the adoption of the patient. For the therapist, relevant issues become whether the principle of confidentiality can be overlooked & the patient told the truth about his heritage; another issue is whether the individual or the whole family is the patient. These & other theoretical problems are analyzed in the light of recent research on family behavior in therapeutic settings. 18 References. D. Dunseath.
