Primary Prevention/Promotion and the Mental Health of the Aging

Author: Bloom, Martin11 School Social Work Virginia Commonwealth U, Richmond 23284

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61605197?accountid=14667

Abstract: A positive approach to the mental health of the aging is given, in contrast to the pathological orientation that permeates the helping professions. This approach involves promoting the strengths of individuals & groups, as well as preventing the predictable risks facing them. This dual orientation is proactive & urges a new perspective in serving the aging. A continuum of programs is suggested: those that promote self-help, where the individual learns to recognize & use his/her own strengths; self-help groups, where persons sharing common risks & potentials aid one another; & secondary-help groups, where both public & private sector organizations help people help themselves. 44 References. Modified AA.

Religion and Genetics: The Possible Effect of Good Pastoral Care on Genetic Counseling Clinics

Author: Weiss, Joan O11 Johns Hopkins Hospital, Baltimore MD 21205

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61047405?accountid=14667

Abstract: When children are born with genetic defects, their parents often believe that they are being punished for some sin, or that they have been "chosen" to guide their impaired child. A strong religious belief can be an effective coping mechanism, but question is raised as to potentially damaging effects as well, eg, the assumption that God will find a cure, leading to refusal of medical therapy. A person's religious beliefs influence his or her attitudes toward a child's genetic disorder, toward eventual acceptance of genetic risks & burdens, & toward future reproductive alternatives. Suggestions are offered on how pastoral counselors can be helpful to those with genetic disorders & their families. 7 References. Modified AA.

Refugee Resettlement: Toward a Conceptual Framework

Author: Moore, Terence M11 Utah State U, Logan 84322

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61605743?accountid=14667

Abstract: Issues & problems in the resettlement of Indochinese refugees in Utah are compared with national & regional information, & their social service needs & service utilization patterns are assessed. A community survey was administered to a random sample of 103 Utah sponsors of Indochinese refugees, & a key informant instrument was administered to the 43 social service agencies in Utah that provide social services to Indochinese refugees. Pre- & post-1979 refugee admissions were examined across demographic characteristics, adjustment patterns, resettlement issues, & social service needs. Among study conclusions were the following: The Indochinese refugee population in Utah paralleled its population in the US in demographic characteristics & patterns of sociocultural adjustment. Utah refugees have not yet completed the cycle of sociocultural adjustment to life in the US, & resettlement has occasioned serious strain. Understanding & use of community social services by refugee sponsors was limited. Recommendations are made for a theory of refugee resettlement & more efficient delivery of social services to the refugees. The importance of mental health services was evident: symptoms of maladjustment & other pathologies among recent refugee arrivals, vulnerable to feelings of depression & loss, must be addressed. Efforts to bring the refugees together through friendship & support groups as substitutes for extended families should be promoted. The training of bilingual & bicultural mental health therapists & aides is recommended; professionals should be given special training in resettlement. Closer collaboration between the federal government & individual states on refugee admission policy & quotas is suggested. 18 References. Modified AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Refugee+Resettlement%3A+Toward+a+Conceptual+Framework&amp;rft.au=Moore%2C+Terence+M&amp;rft.aulast=Moore&amp;rft.aufirst=Terence&amp;rft.date=1982-04-01&amp;rft.volume=8&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=8&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

The Developmental Process of Parish Social Ministries: A Decade of Experience

Author: Joseph, M Vincentia11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61601498?accountid=14667

Abstract: A phase-specific analysis of the development of agency-affiliated social ministries in the local parish-neighborhood over the past decade is presented. Agency-affiliated programs, eg, the Catholic Charities agency, combine or network the resources of the local parish church with the diocesan or regional church structures to perform social service/social action functions. The six-stage model presented reflects the concept of systems change holding that as growth occurs, it is often accompanied by conflict from both within the system (the agency-parish network) & from outside (external forces, eg, the larger neighborhood community). The impact of resistance or opposition forces as well as of supportive or positive forces is considered, the effects at agency & local operational levels are discussed, & phases of development are outlined. It is concluded that the current social, economic, & political climate compels efforts to strengthen, expand, & enhance this approach. 7 References. Modified AA.

The Rights of Handicapped Children: A Challenge to Social Service Development

Author: Constable, Robert T11 Jane Addams School Social Work U Illinois, Chicago Circle 60680

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61441000?accountid=14667

Stepfamilies: Situational Problems

Author: Wolf, Perry L11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61601999?accountid=14667

Abstract: More than 6 million children presently live in stepfamily situations, most typically in situations in which the stepparent is the father. The time that stepfamilies are formed by remarriage is critical for family members, who are often unsure of new role boundaries; as such, it is a time when social work intervention can be helpful in resolving social, practical, & emotional problems of those involved. Some typical problems faced by members of the newly formed family are described, eg, children's expectations of stepparental behavior, the stepparent's uncertainty about his or her authority, & adaptation to new kinship & social networks. 23 References. D. Dunseath.

The Health Care Policy Pendulum: An Ethical Perspective (1981 O'Grady Award Winner)

Author: Conrad, Ann Patrick11 9727 Mount Pisgan Rd, Silver Spring MD 20903

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61601289?accountid=14667

Abstract: Based on social work experience, the escalating interest in ethical issues in the US is noted. Although scholarly literature is developing, particularly around ethical dilemmas in direct practice, there is only beginning utilization of value inclusive frameworks for analyzing public policy. Recent shifts in health care policy are analyzed for an ethical perspective utilizing an ethical model for decision making based on the principles of proportionalism. Health care legislation & its related underlying philosophical rationale are conceptualized in terms of discrete but overlapping phases. The expansion phase, the period from the early 1960s through the mid-1970s, was characterized by bills on community-based care, prevention, training, & research, based on a philosophy that persons are entitled to all that is necessary to promote health. The period of cost containment, during the 1970s, was characterized by frequency of regulatory & planning activity, peer review, & increase of copayments for medical care, & was accompanied by a more conservative understanding of the obligation to insure the right to a healthy existence. The current situation, with increasing block grants, termed a period of delegation of responsibility, is justified on the grounds of competition & free enterprise, & results in a dilemma of entitlement vs competition. The various value hierarchies undergirding these two approaches are identified, the importance placed by social work & other helping professions on the common good is highlighted, drawbacks for professionals & quality client service are discussed, & the long & circuitous route to the common good when the competition approach is taken is pointed out. 2 Figures, 27 References. Modified AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=The+Health+Care+Policy+Pendulum%3A+An+Ethical+Perspective+%281981+O%27Grady+Award+Winner%29&amp;rft.au=Conrad%2C+Ann+Patrick&amp;rft.aulast=Conrad&amp;rft.aufirst=Ann&amp;rft.date=1982-01-01&amp;rft.volume=8&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=25&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Social Policy in Relation to the Community Development Block Grant Process

Author: Nover, Aimee R11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61624365?accountid=14667

Abstract: An attempt by a Md day care center to obtain funds from the federal Community Development Block Grant Program precipitated unexpected debate about the appropriateness of the use of these funds for day care. The event is used to illustrate social policy issues relevant to eligibility for federal assistance. Issues discussed include the following: (1) the role of the local government in establishing community priorities; (2) effects of citizen participation in the application for funding; & (3) use of block grant funds for social work & social services. Combating the Scapegoat in Family Therapy: Selected Strategies

Author: Schuchts, Robert A1; David, James R1 Florida State U, Tallahassee 32306

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61574176?accountid=14667

Abstract: Strategies for alleviating scapegoating tendencies in family therapy are examined, focusing on the rigidity of relationships within the family unit when a member is labeled as problematic. A child is most likely to be advanced as the scapegoat & submitted for treatment by the adults; the need for the therapist to avoid conforming to family communication patterns & expectations is emphasized. Rather, he or she must assume an authoritative, quasi-adversary position within the unit & utilize strategies of communications remodeling, reforming alliances & coalitions, producing stress in a controlled fashion, & assigning special tasks to improve problem-solving skills. Means of introducing & monitoring such solutions are detailed, with particular attention to reinforcing, displacing, & assigning paradoxical tasks. Eventually, a cooperative, "coalition" relationship between family & therapist is seen as emerging; termination in such cases is based on the family's sense of success & adjustment. 16 References. Modified Author Summary.

A Multi-Theoretical Approach to Adolescent Delinquency

Author: Baker, Patricia K S11 9621 Culver, Kensington MD 20895

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61588433?accountid=14667

Abstract: Findings of the major studies on adolescent delinquency are reviewed & a model is developed using four theories to explain them. Cultural deviance, social control, & strain theory are discussed. Although social control theory has the greatest explanatory capability, no one theory adequately accounts for the research findings. According to psychodynamic theory, the major developmental task of the adolescent is separation & individuation. It is hypothesized that the delinquent act may be an act against parental control & toward development of personal identity. A model employing psychodynamic theory as well as social control, cultural deviance, & strain theory is presented. Implications for mental health practitioners, correctional officials, & further research are discussed. 1 Figure, 31 References. Modified AA.

Facing the Critical Issues of Social Security

Author: Berman, Jules11 School Social Work U Maryland, College Park 20742

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61635730?accountid=14667

Abstract: Some problems threatening the financial stability of the Social Security system are identified, including inflation, Medicare costs, rising unemployment, demographic changes, & the trend toward early retirement. If the system is not to collapse, the government must find new funding sources, restrict eligibility, or reduce benefits. The feasibility of each of these alternatives is considered. 2 References. D. Reflections on Retirement

Author: McAdoo, Lucile11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61625370?accountid=14667

Abstract: Retired professionals may manage life after work more ably than other retired persons by having more disciplined minds & more carefully defined expectations of the retirement years. Former professionals face many of the same problems -- eg, declining health, economic restrictions, loss of loved ones -- but attitudes of intellectual commitment having become habitual over many years, professional retired persons may sustain a greater interest in living. They may also preserve a more highly developed sense of the self & feelings of personal & societal responsibility. 3 References. D. Dunseath.

Assessing Catholic Purpose in American Catholic Higher Education

Author: Nuesse, C Joseph11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61043842?accountid=14667

Abstract: Certain aspects of Catholic purpose must be noted in a sociological analysis of Catholic higher education: (1) Catholic purpose is given primacy in socialization; (2) in Catholic self-understanding, any apparent opposition between Catholic & educational aims is to be resolved by analysis & ordering, not by compromise; & (3) educational effort is expected to be respectful of both the integrity of subject matter & the particular demands of educational development. US Catholic institutions of higher education, which are to a large extent unique in the world, share the nature of & confront the issues that are found in higher education in general, but are called upon to face the deeper challenges of a social system in which religion has been progressively neutralized, not least in the relatively autonomous & secularized modern U. AA

Ethical Considerations in the Treatment of Severely Defective Newborns

Author: Fischer, Wendy C11 3253 Lothian Rd, Fairfax VA 22031

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61588893?accountid=14667

Abstract: Ethical issues surrounding the treatment of severely defective newborns are examined. Through the use of a hypothetical case, these questions are raised: By what process & according to what criteria should it be decided whether a severely defective newborn should be kept alive? What is the kind of life that is to be respected? Who should make the decision for the newborn? Literature pertaining to the issues involved is reviewed. Dilemmas concerning the welfare of the infant are presented, & the question of life vs meaningful life is explored. Costs to the family & to society, & decision making about allocating finite resources are also discussed. In addition, opinions on whether parents, MDs, other professionals, or society should make the decisions are examined. Finally, ethical options from the point of view of a social worker in a medical setting are presented. It is concluded that the ultimate decision about intervention in these cases would depend on an assessment of factors crucial to whether the child's potential for meaningful life could be realized. 15 References. Modified AA.

The Judaeo-Christian Tradition of Family Life: Fit and Misfit in the '80s

Author: Peachey, Paul11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61082497?accountid=14667

Abstract: US society appears to be increasingly moving beyond the Judeo-Christian family tradition. The proposition that this departure derives from the Judeo-Christian tradition itself is difficult to test, given the manifold, sometimes contradictory, forms within that tradition -- eg, patriarchy, polygamy, & avowals of sexual equality. Viewed phenomenologically (whatever the theological assessment), it can be argued that the views of conjugality & sexual equality at the heart of Judeo-Christian spirituality have been a source of ferment in Western history. To invoke this tradition in support of familial conservatism (patriarchal monogamy, M dominance, simple identification of women with the domestic sphere, etc) is, therefore, indefensible. The Judeo-Christian tradition is at odds with the trivialization of conjugality & sexuality in US society owing to the former's high conception of human beings & human integrity, not for reasons of dogma or institutional control. The weakening of traditional structures, though manifested as a "breakdown," provides a context within which responsible personhood & sexual equality are possible. 32 References. Modified AA.

The White House Conference on Families: Process, Policies, and Politics

Author: Carr, John L11 Center Community Change, Washington DC 20013

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61542981?accountid=14667

Abstract: The White House Conferences on Families were held in Baltimore, Md, Minneapolis, Minn, & Los Angeles, Calif, in June & July 1980. Their delegates reflected the wide cultural, ethnic, & SE diversity of the US, & they showed a general unanimity about what issues were significant: economic problems, government callousness to family needs, child care, education, health, & employment. Of the delegates 13% were single parents, 25+% were of an ethnic or racial minority, 5% were handicapped, & 10% were of families earning less than $8,000 per year. Some examples of Conference recommendations that have been acted upon since the conventions are discussed, including: issues of the workplace, drug & alcohol abuse, tax policies, home health care, problems of the handicapped, the religious community, & establishment of a federal Office for Families. Appendix. D. Dunseath.

Advocacy for Families: The Catholic Coordinating Committee for the White House Conference on Families

Author: Mahoney, Charlotte M

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61584116?accountid=14667

Abstract: A review of the Catholic Church's role in the 1980 White House Conference on Families, as expressed through the Catholic Coordinating Committee. The Committee refused any form of political participation in the Conference, recognizing that families themselves would lose out in ideological contests. It adopted the role of responsible family advocate, evincing concern for all areas of family life, ie, economic, social, religious, educational, & moral. It helped created a National Office for Families, which would serve to evaluate the strengths & weaknesses of family policies. A review of the evolution of the Coordinating Committee is provided, its goals are broadly identified, & its recommendations for the Final Report of the National Task Force are specified. D. Dunseath.

Who Wants a National Policy on Children and Families?

Author: McCarthy, John D11 Boys Town Center Study Youth Development Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61583239?accountid=14667

Abstract: A growing movement is apparent to create a national policy for the US on children & families. A critical analysis of this movement is presented. Movements involving treatment of children have often seen them as symbols rather than examining their actual needs. Presently, a large professional class exists that seeks to shape public policy in accord with its own values, & sometimes finds itself in conflict with the general public. This is particularly true for family policy proposals, which are characterized by support for increased state intervention in the family, with the implied effect of making the family less self-sufficient. There is reason for opposition to this set of policies, & to the use of children's interests as a policy symbol. W. H. Stoddard.

Political Compromise: The Developmental Task of Societal Understanding in Adolescence

Author: Furth, Hans1; McConville, Kathleen1 Boys Town Center Study Youth Development Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61526036?accountid=14667

Abstract: Understanding of opposing views & realistic compromise solutions for 12 political & legal situations was explored in 72 adolescents, aged 14-19. Their explanations were rated on a 3-point scale in terms of mention of opposing views & of likely societal-legal procedures. In 3 increasing age groups, 1-rated responses dropped (42%, 31%, 4%) & 3-rated responses increased (20%, 31%, 66%). Four aspects of political understanding were proposed: recognition of individual rights, articulation of other (different from personal) viewpoints, need for reasonable compromise, & separation of legal from conventional-moral regulations. 1 Table. AA.

Friendship and Development

Author: Youniss, James11 Boys Town Center Study Youth Development Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61554947?accountid=14667

Abstract: Recent evidence showing how friendship, as distinguished from peer relations, is the source of children's learning cooperation & mutual respect is reviewed. The development of these positive social functions is plotted for the period beginning with school age through early adolescence. Data gathered through interviews with about 1,000 children (Youniss, J., Parents and Peers in Social Development, Chicago: U of Chicago Press, 1980) indicate that friendship develops differently than relations with parents during this period. Relations with parents are seen as emphasizing conformity & unilateral respect, whereas friendship contributes more positively to social moral development. The results apply equally to personal adjustment, insofar as friendship is a special ground for claiming one's own weaknesses & for seeing how one's own talents can be used for mutual aid. AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Friendship+and+Development&amp;rft.au=Youniss%2C+James&amp;rft.aulast=Youniss&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rft.date=1981-01-01&amp;rft.volume=7&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=35&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Religious Development among Adolescents

Author: Potvin, Raymond H1; Lee, Che-Fu1 Boys Town Center Study Youth Development Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61045316?accountid=14667

Abstract: Durkheimian & Piagetian theory are integrated to explain adolescent religious development. The resulting hypotheses are tested with data from a national probability sample of 1,121 US youths aged 13-18 who were interviewed in 1965. At 13-14, the impact of peers is minimal, & religious practice, mainly related to parental religions, has a greater influence on internal religiousness than the reverse process. At 15-16, adolescents begin to coconstruct with peers worldviews impacting on internal religiousness that at these ages have a greater influence on practice than the reverse process. At 17-18, the influence of practice on internal religiousness regains its former primacy. Adolescents tend to reconcile early religiousness attained on the basis of authority relations with those modifications of religiousness attained on the basis of meanings coconstructed with peers. 1 Figure, 1 Appendix, 40 References. Modified AA.

Behavioral Practice in a Social Service Agency: A Practitioner Reports

Author: Breidenbach, Dennis C11 Catholic Social Services, Dayton OH 45401

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61554574?accountid=14667

Abstract: The behavioral approach to social work practice relies on a model involving four phases of activity: assessment, modification, evaluation, & follow-up. Review of 73 cases handled through this approach, in the course of personal agency practice, gives evidence of its applicability to a wide range of problems. While a significant investment of time & some commitment of material resources are required, these appear to be justified by the benefits. Ethical guidelines are needed for this approach; a set of guidelines appropriate to open-setting practice is suggested. A number of supportive conditions are needed for application of this model to be effective. W. H. Stoddard.

Abortion: Toward Developing a Policy in a Catholic Social Service Agency

Author: Dendinger, Donald C1; Mathern, Timothy1 Coll Public Affairs & Community Service School Social Work U Nebraska, Omaha 68182

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61580607?accountid=14667

Abstract: With regard to the currently controversial issue of abortion, personnel in Catholic social service agencies are caught in the dilemma of conflicting policies -- those of the Catholic Church & of the National Assoc of Social Workers. It is suggested that the issue be addressed more directly & clearly by a policy statement from each agency. An example of such a policy statement appropriate to a Catholic social service agency is furnished as a means of facilitating the development of policies by agencies confronted with this issue. Modified Author Conclusion.

Hospice Care: Rebirth of a Concept

Author: Shevlin, Kathleen M11 School Medicine Georgetown U, Washington DC 20057

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61435633?accountid=14667

Abstract: The hospice movement seeks to offer care to terminally ill patients, especially cancer patients, in a way that preserves their social & family relationships & enables them & their families to deal effectively with the emotional problems of death. The experience of the Catholic Georgetown U Hospital's hospice program is examined, & guidelines followed in the program are outlined. J. F. Potter (Evaluation and Research in the Hospice, paper presented at the First Annual National Hospice Organization Meeting & Fifth National Hospice Symposium, Washington, DC, Oct 1978) notes the need to evaluate such areas of operation as patient selection, decisions concerning treatment, clinical judgment in the hospice, personnel functioning, the place of thanatology, & possible exploitation for financial gain; these issues must be dealt with for effective hospice functioning. The Catholic Church's view of death offers a basis for effective ministry to the dying. It is desirable that home care be integrated with hospice care as fully as possible. W. H. Stoddard.

Public Policies and the Aged: Some Additional Questions

Author: Vinyard, Dale11 Wayne State U, Detroit MI 48202

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61538156?accountid=14667

Abstract: In the last several decades, the US government has made a substantial commitment to the aged in policies & programs, but these policies generally treat the aged as a homogeneous group, not recognizing the existence of different needs, particularly those of the most disadvantaged aged. Thus, many policies have simply perpetuated existing differences & have not substantially alleviated the condition of the aged poor. Race, sex, education, work history, & other factors may be at least as important as age in determining an aged individual's condition. While many efforts to aid the aged are flawed & incomplete, on the whole they have been treated more generously & sympathetically than other disadvantaged groups in society. In many ways, the aged have been among the major beneficiaries of the welfare state. Modified Author Conclusion.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Public+Policies+and+the+Aged%3A+Some+Additional+Questions&amp;rft.au=Vinyard%2C+Dale&amp;rft.aulast=Vinyard&amp;rft.aufirst=Dale&amp;rft.date=1980-04-01&amp;rft.volume=6&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.spage=31&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Economic Justice: Which Way from Here?

Author: Brannon, Gerard11 American Council Life Insurance, 277 Park Ave New York NY 10017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61542948?accountid=14667

Abstract: An attempt is made to clarify some issues confronting an attempt to apply the doctrines of the Roman Catholic Church to economic justice issues in the contemporary US. Historical review shows that the twentieth century has developed an institution, the welfare state, that solves many problems that were the concerns of the Church in the nineteenth century; but new issues have emerged. These include the dimensions of economic philosophy, politics, & such specific areas as taxation, social security, welfare, regulation, & full employment. In the long run, forming a moral position requires better understanding of how social choices are made. In the short run, there is a need for moral positions on specific contemporary issues. Attention should be given to evaluating the probable performance of the political system in dealing with those issues held to be its proper concern. Modified Author Summary.

A Call to Harvest, Ministry to America

Author: Hubbard, Howard11 Catholic Diocese Albany, NY 12207

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61553947?accountid=14667

Abstract: Keynote address to the sixty-fifth annual meeting of the National Conference of Catholic Charities, Kansas City, Mo, 11-13 Oct 1979. Basic principles underlying the operation of Catholic charities include: that these charities are an extension of the mission of Jesus in present conditions; that charitable work is a ministry; & that individual persons have transcendent dignity & must be the focal point of this ministry. A danger to be avoided is a preoccupation with organization that prevents communication with individuals. Personal preoccupations with advancing one's own interests or goals can be a major source of problems. If these difficulties are to be avoided, the role of faith in the life & work of charitable workers must be developed as fully as possible. W. H. Stoddard.

Subsidiarity and Voluntarism in Mass Society

Author: Dechert, Charles R11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61601841?accountid=14667

Abstract: An important historical development of the past several centuries has been the creation of a mass society in which regularity is increasingly imposed by both public & private agencies. This development makes full return to local community impossible. At the same time, voluntary associations & relationships persist, & offer a basis for humanizing the social machinery. A growing awareness of the limits of state intervention is leading toward renewed reliance on voluntarism. The failures of the advanced nations offer a motive for reexamination of many of the institutions & practices of other nations, & for hesitation about imposing Western approaches on these nations. Modified Author Conclusion.

Social Work's Identity Crisis: A Christian Anthropological Response

Author: Hess, Joseph J, Jr11 Catholic Social Services, Philadelphia PA 19104

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61435602?accountid=14667

Abstract: Social work as a profession is now entering a crisis of identity; the possible response to this crisis by Catholic social work is considered. Conflict exists at theoretical, practical, & ethical levels. A central concept for social work must be "will to meaning," as defined within the conceptual framework of Christian anthropology. This will to meaning is in fact the core of the crisis of social work itself as it now exists. W. H. Stoddard.

Adoption 1979: Sleeping Beauty Awakes

Author: Dukette, Rita11 School Social Work Loyola U, Chicago IL 60611

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61544134?accountid=14667

Abstract: Following examination of the historical development of the institution of adoption, current developments on the issue of confidentiality vs openness of adoption records are addressed by considering the probable future implications for all parties to the adoption, & for the practices of adoption agencies if the current legal constraints on openness are removed. Both the benefits & possible hazards of openness are presented. Changes in adoption practices that a changed legal context may require, & that will still protect the adoptee, the birth parents, & the adoptive parents, are suggested. Modified AA.

Origins: New Challenges for Adoption Agencies

Author: Cashman, Frances11 Catholic Charities, 645 West Randolph St Chicago IL 60606

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61538279?accountid=14667

Abstract: Changes in social attitudes during the 1960s & 1970s included a dramatic intensity in the conflict between the "right to know" & the "right to confidentiality" as it affected members of the adoption triad. While Catholic Charities of Chicago has been offering postadoption counseling since 1956, the staff time required to help members of the adoption triad deal with their conflicts, anxieties, & anger has increased significantly. Experience gained from the establishment of adoptive parents clubs in 1957 & an adoptive parents guild in 1974, as well as biannual adoption conferences since 1959 to provide a channel for an ongoing educational program, has assisted agency staff in maintaining contacts, provided insight in the problems of all members of the adoption triad, & enabled the agency to adjust & adapt its services appropriately. Experiences in reunion problems are narrated & statistics are provided documenting inquiries made by adoptees, natural parents, & adoptive parents. Recommendations are offered to help agencies deal with the problems of the adoption triad. 3 Tables. AA.

The Adoption of Special Needs Children: Theory versus Practice

Author: Tucker, Maida S11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61580546?accountid=14667

Abstract: Many agencies concerned with adoption regard children with special needs as unlikely to be adopted, & therefore needing foster care. It is beginning to be recognized, however, that such children can find adoptive parents if the appropriate innovative means are used. Procedures needed include: review of caseloads of children in foster care; review of adoption criteria; familiarity with subsidized adoptions; evaluation of innovative recruitment techniques; extension of the education of adoption workers; & coordination of activities with adoptive parent groups. A questionnaire covering education, recruitment, screening, subsidies, foster care, & adoption criteria was completed by the 18 agencies in the Washington, DC, metropolitan area. Agencies fall short of optimal implementation of the recommended procedures, doing best in foster care & education, & worst in recruitment & subsidies. Effects of various factors on implementation success are evaluated. Relationship with child advocacy groups & agency jurisdiction are the most significant factors. 3 Charts. W. H. Stoddard.

Anonymity in the Adoption Process: The Legal Aspects

Author: Fox, William F, Jr11 Law School Catholic U, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61564300?accountid=14667

Abstract: Legal issues incident to a request by an adopted person for his or her original birth records are discussed, with particular attention paid to the claim advanced by some adopted persons that they have a constitutional right to see their birth records even in the face of state statutes requiring that such records be sealed. It is difficult if not impossible to sustain a constitutional basis for access, but most adoptees could have access for any legitimate purpose if the sealed-records statutes were only slightly modified. Given the noted reluctance of the US Supreme Court to discern constitutionally based right of privacy, a statutory right of access may be the only meaningful alternative. AA.

Moral Issues in the Adoption Process

Author: Finan, William J11 U Dallas, Irving TX 75061

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61602572?accountid=14667

Abstract: In an ethical analysis of selected issues in the adoption process, criteria are developed for information sharing among parties to adoption; it is argued that adoptees, biological parents, & adoptive parents all have rights. The basic premise is that personal privacy be respected, & confidentiality observed. Information about biological parents &/or adoptees cannot be provided without explicit approval of the persons involved, except in cases of urgent need. Arguments on other issues include: that potential adoptive parents ought not to be questioned about their contraceptive practices; that fertility testing should always respect personal dignity & privacy; & that the possibility of adoption by homosexual couples ought not to be ruled out a priori. Modified AA.

Applied Research in Social Work: Conceptions of Scientific Practice

Author: Bloom, Martin11 Virginia Commonwealth U, Richmond 23284

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61435716?accountid=14667

Abstract: The new fusion in social work between research & empirical practice is traced to a number of developments in the field, including: diversification of social work models into dynamic, behavioral, & other approaches; a rather recent emphasis on evaluation research; & generally increased attention to issues of sex, age, race, & SC within societies. Observation of scientific practice in social work discloses several common dimensions: (1) use of classical research data in practice; (2) use of client-based information in practice; (3) single-system designs; (4) use of theory in practice; (5) more attention to effectiveness & efficiency; & (6) educational implications. These issues are discussed, & the significance of client participation in modern social work practice is analyzed. 1 Figure. D. Dunseath.

Aging: A Theological Perspective

Author: Curran, Charles E11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20064

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61580481?accountid=14667

Abstract: The meaning of aging, rather than programmatic aspects of the question, are discussed from the limited perspective of Roman Catholic theology. Aging raises the question of death, which is viewed in the light of a fivefold Christian stance involving the realities of creation, sin, incarnation, redemption, & resurrection destiny. There is, consequently, both discontinuity & continuity between this life & the next; thus the inadequacy of a peak or slope view of human existence, which sees aging & death only in terms of loss & diminishment. Human experience can support theological reflection on life after death by seeing it in continuity with the most distinctively human trait -- growing self-encounter & expanding relationships with God & others; these aspects should be present in the aging process. Death is somewhat paradigmatic of other crises & growth situations in human existence, in which it is necessary to die in the confines of the present in order to enter into a stage of greater sharing in life. Thus the theological concept of the paschal mystery gives meaning to death & to aging, & accounts for both growth & decline associated with aging. Such a Christian understanding is opposed to a purely technological view of the human, which attributes meaning only to the performance of external works or to financial productivity. Modified AA.

The National Catholic School of Social Service: Some Reminiscences

Author: Mohler, Dorothy A11 National Conference Catholic Charities, 1346 Connecticut Ave NW Washington DC 20036

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61564482?accountid=14667

Abstract: In 1918, the US Catholic hierarchy established in Washington, DC, a training school, popularly known as Clifton, to prepare women for war & reconstruction work. After the war, the school was renamed the National Catholic School of Social Service, & became a graduate school of social work sponsored & supported for twenty-five years by the National Council of Catholic Women. Affiliated with the Catholic U of America, it was unique among schools of social work in the US in maintaining a residence requirement for its students. In 1934, the Catholic U established a graduate school of social work for men. Stressing the importance of training leaders, from its beginning the school included a doctoral program in social work, the third oldest in the US. Development of close relationships between the men's & women's schools culminated in a merger in 1947. Prominent persons associated with the schools are noted. Modified AA.

Professional Competency, Autonomy, and Job Satisfaction among Social Workers in an Appalachian Rural Area

Author: Kim, Dong I1; Boo, Sung L; Wheeler, Alban1 West Virginia U, Morgantown 26506

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61435714?accountid=14667

Abstract: Recent data on Ur social workers examined by R. G. Meinert ("Professional Satisfaction of Social Workers," Social Work, 1975, 20, 64-65) show a generally high level of career satisfaction. To assess job satisfaction among Ru social workers, questionnaires returned by social work professionals in eastern Ky (N = 97) were analyzed using various instruments; eg, job satisfaction was measured through a Likert-type scale, professional self-image & work autonomy were assessed through discrepancy measures to level personality differences, & competencies were measured on a self-diagnosis index formed in 1976 at the U of Montana. Background variables of sex, education, & income were also incorporated. Results show that most Ru social workers are quite satisfied with their work, with a mean score of 31.3 on a scale of 10-40, & that they practice at a fairly high level of competence, with a mean score of 5.6 on a scale of 1-7. 6 Tables. D. Dunseath.

Natural Family Planning: Father Bernard Haring's Position: An Essay Review

Author: May, William E11 School Religious Studies Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61538129?accountid=14667

Abstract: Bernard Haring (see SOPODA 2:1/D0612) affirmed that the rhythm method of controlling conception increases the chance of fertilization from "overripe" gametic cells, & in so doing increases the incidence of spontaneous abortions & the risk of having deformed children. Haring's conclusions have been challenged by several critics, including Thomas W. Hilgers ("Human Reproduction: Three Issues for the Moral Theologian," Theological Studies, 1977, 38, 136-152). Hilgers's argument is described, & the issue of voluntary sterilization raised by Haring is discussed from a Roman Catholic point of view. D. Dunseath.

The Role of Healing Prayer in the Helping Professions

Author: Gatza, Marie11 Archdiocese Philadelphia Catholic Social Services, 222 North 17th St PA 19103

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61548036?accountid=14667

Abstract: The use of prayer is suggested in the helping professions, specifically in the Catholic Charities Movement. The intent is to describe healing prayer & its growing use among health & mental health professionals to augment & enrich their professional skills. The American Military Community as a Testing Ground for the Development of Social Welfare Policy

Author: McNeil, John S1; Wright, Roosevelt1 Graduate School Social Work U Texas, Arlington 76019

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61569626?accountid=14667

Abstract: There is a positive relationship between the formulation, development, & implementation of social policies in the US military community & in the broader US society. As a result of the association between these policy areas, it is concluded that military social policies are the forerunners of social policies in the broader society. Additionally, what has transpired in the military community relative to the development & implementation of social welfare policies & programs has been extremely beneficial to the masses in society. US social policy writers have tended to focus upon the "bullets vs butter" economic arguments of military policy & have failed to perceive other policy developments. British social policy scholars & analysts tend to view the relationship between society's involvement in war & the development & implementation of its social policies as complementary functions. Cited & supported is the contention of British policy analysts. Modified AA.

Assault on Clinical Practice

Author: Berl, Fred; Chescheir, Martha

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61599655?accountid=14667

Abstract: During the last decade, clinical family & children's services have been battered by many forces. One reason for this is that clinical programs have relied almost exclusively on psychodynamic treatment methods, discovered a century ago when social systems were fixed & stable. With the advent of advanced technology & the growing disenchantment with social institutions of all kinds, the social order has become increasingly unstable & unpredictable. This has increased the severity of the kinds of disorders clinicians are called upon to treat. The field has a dual responsibility to attend both to social needs & to individual clients. A two-directional model is suggested: improving social conditions, & facilitating individual & interpersonal growth. The person-situation paradigm will become inoperative without clinical services to family & children. Interhuman contact will be reestablished by examining & understanding the kinds of problems that individuals & families experience, thereby enabling them to hold together. Modified Author Summary.

Organizational Change: A Return to Neighborhood Social Service Centers

Author: Underhill, Patricia11 U Colorado, Denver 80202

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61569276?accountid=14667

Abstract: Neighborhood social services are not a new phenomenon, but the trend in the past few decades to centralize social services has militated against the more personalized neighborhood service center. Efforts to economize on administrative costs, personnel, & other resources have contributed to the centralization process. However, with the new neighborhood team concept, an attempt was made to decentralize a portion of the social services. The change process that evolved was unique because: (1) both the stimuli & the means for the planned change emerged from the agency & its constituents who participated in all phases of the process, including planning & decision making; & (2) the conflicts or tensions usually inherent in a major organizational transformation were minimal. Since the neighborhood teams were to consist of interdisciplinary specialists, caseworkers, volunteer specialists, community organizers, & one other person depending upon the assessed needs of the target area, the problem of dual supervision arose -- administrative supervision by the team leader, & supervision according to professional specialty. The participant study surfaced additional problems that needed to be addressed before successive teams could become operational. AA.

Natural Family Planning: The Contribution of Fertility Awareness to Body-Person Integration

Author: Klaus, Hanna11 Holy Cross Hospital Silver Spring, 1500 Forest Glen Rd MD 20910

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61548203?accountid=14667

Abstract: The predominant approach to the prevention of teenage pregnancy is one of recruiting teenagers into contraceptive programs. In spite of great efforts, the large portion of abortions in the US is among teenagers; the numbers lead one to think that failure to utilize contraception may be deeper than mere nonavailability. While pregnancy was evidently elected at some level of decision making, the numbers of abortions suggest that these girls usually do not wish to give birth. The current thrust of technological contraception is to separate the act of sex from the act of procreation. Reviewed is psychoanalytic theory, particularly that of H. Deutsch, which suggests that the act of procreation is already contained in human coital activity. While the technological contraceptives all operate from the psychological level to facilitate sexual activity while preventing pregnancy, it is suggested that part of the adolescent search for identity is to establish gender identity. Part of gender identity is to experience the body as real. Fertility awareness & the contemporary fertility acceptance methods -- ovulation & symptothermal methods -- are briefly described. These methods have a failure rate of 1%. The learning process connected with one's body language requires time, support, & usually discussion in order to come to grips with the feelings engendered by the periodic abstinence inherent in use of these methods when pregnancy avoidance is desired. By the same token, these methods can be used to achieve pregnancy. They are, therefore, not methods of pregnancy prevention but rather of achieving sexual responsibility in exercising procreative choice. A number of providers of pregnancy prevention services for teenagers have been hesitant to "trust" girls with the responsibility of natural family planning methods, while expecting them to engage in sexual intercourse. It is suggested that instead of protecting people against the consequences of their own decisions, it would be better to explain the powers of the body to adolescents, to show them the long-term implications of their behavior, & to challenge them to rise to the fullness of their capabilities. Fertility is not a disease & does not require a medical model to cope with it. On the other hand, it is absurd to teach that an act of the body (coitus) should not have somatic consequences. Modified AA.

A "Peer-Group" Model for Supervision

Author: Bardill, Donald R11 School Social Work Florida State U, Tallahassee 32306

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61500707?accountid=14667

Abstract: The peer group model for supervision is based on an eight-year project involving nineteen different supervisory groups who counseled families at Walter Reed Army Medical Center. Among the rationales for such an approach are: (1) that the traditional one-to-one approach has proved ineffective for supervision of family cases; (2) that the structure of the group supervision model can usually be devised to show family dynamics; (3) that the modeling available in a group setting is a powerful learning tool; & (4) that through analysis of various cases, participants can acquire knowledge of other families' dynamics. The basic philosophical tenets for the model are that: (A) each participant is responsible for his/her own words, thoughts, & actions in the sessions; (B) participation & sharing are the primary bases for an effective supervisory process; & (C) the purpose of the sessions must be explicit if they are to be productive. A list of group accords, or rules, is included. P. Montgomery.

Family Policy and the Carter Administration

Author: Antler, Stephen11 Boston U, MA 02215

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61566337?accountid=14667

Abstract: Critics of contemporary social policy contend that the categorical programs developed over the past two decades do not resolve the problems to which they are directed; instead they spawn additional programs for newly defined social problems. Dissatisfaction with piecemeal social reform has turned the attention of many policy analysts to the idea of developing comprehensive social policies on behalf of improving family life. Despite preelection promises to stress family well-being as the cornerstone of the Carter administration policy, little effort has been forthcoming to promote necessary social welfare programs. Though momentum for family policies has been growing, strongly held & diverse conceptions of family life, differing views about the role of government toward families, & concern about the costs of comprehensive policies have retarded their development. Strong leadership is needed to create coalitions which can provide support for family policies. Based on the first two years of the Carter administration, it does not appear that the necessary leadership will be forthcoming. Modified AA.

Love of God in Action, Our Heritage and Our Hope

Author: Higgins, George G

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61455936?accountid=14667

Abstract: It has been charged that the Catholic Charities have focused on issues of personal or family concern, leaving the problem of social reform to others. At the time of the first Catholic Charities Conference in 1910, the Catholic Church was extremely busy with internal affairs, & did not turn its energy outward for some years; however, during the late nineteenth & early twentieth centuries, the Church coped with the mass immigration of millions of Catholics, which was a remarkable contribution to American public life. The role of the Church in social reform is traced from these beginnings to the present. Current issues such as the impact of California's Proposition 13 are of great interest to the Church. P. Montgomery.

A Christian Perspective on the Reality of Illegal Immigration

Author: Deck, Allan Figueroa11 Centro Pastoral Guadalupe, 541 E Central Ave Santa Ana CA 92707

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61565157?accountid=14667

Abstract: Recent studies of illegal Mexican immigration are juxtaposed with the social teachings of the Roman Catholic Church on migrants. The biblical concept regarding the special care & consideration due the alien or stranger is outlined, & papal pronouncements on the subject highlighting the Catholic Church's insistence on the fundamental human right to migrate out of economic need or to flee persecution are traced. The Church's approach is an international one, reflecting a much keener insight into the phenomenon of migration than do US attitudes & perceptions. The inherent racism, discrimination, & jingoism of US immigration policies against Hispanics, especially Mexicans, over the past several decades are exposed. The causes of Mexican migration to the US are to be found in the policy decisions of international economic elites, & in US economic policy toward Mexico, but the Church's main concern is with US treatment of illegal immigrants, which is neither just nor Christian. Modified AA.

Commonalities in Social Work and Personnel Work

Author: Mulholland, Elizabeth

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61551995?accountid=14667

Abstract: Social work & personnel work are both people-helping professions. Social workers enter the realm of personnelists when they assist clients with workplace problems. Personnelists act as "social workers" when they help frustrated job applicants with feelings of disappointment & anger, or older employees with fears about retirement. These & other similarities are illustrated by a description of the Clergy Personnel Program of the Archdiocese of Baltimore, which provides clergy members with career guidance, counseling, crisis intervention, & preretirement & retirement services. P. Montgomery.

Ethnicity, Immigration and American Catholic History

Author: Gleason, Philip1; Salvaterra, David1 U Notre Dame, IN 46556

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61546334?accountid=14667

Abstract: A survey of the role played by ethnic groups & immigrants within US Catholicism throughout its history. The church is viewed as an "institutional immigrant" -- as an institution it underwent much the same experiences as did individual immigrants. Such status created many of the problems US churchmen had to deal with in regard to their immigrant flock. The wide diversity of experiences, as well as the similarities among the various ethnic groups, are examined by means of traditional historical sources. While much more favorable to its immigrant flock than proponents of the new ethnicity claim, the church -- often acting from historically conditioned circumstances -- compiled a far from perfect record in the treatment of its immigrant members. AA.

The Individuality-Groupness Effect: Phenomenology, Social Values and Clinical Applications

Author: Falck, Hans S11 Virginia Commonwealth U, Richmond 23220

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61455801?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of the integration of personality & social network concepts, which provides a further elaboration of the individuality-groupness (I-G) effect as a synthesizing construct of person & group. Supporting this concept are psychoanalytic object-relations theory & symbolic interactionism. The I-G effect is discussed phenomenologically, from the standpoint of social values & in terms of clinical applications, from the standpoint of normal human development, & from the standpoint of psychopathology & social interaction in abnormal situations. Modified AA.

Consumers on Boards of Catholic Charities Agencies: An Analysis of Selected Values and Attitudes of Board Members toward the Admission of Consumers to Governing Boards

Author: Kellner, Raymond E11 Louisiana State U, Baton Rouge 70803

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61500276?accountid=14667

Abstract: In 1972, the Study Cadre of the National Conference of Catholic Charities urged that recipients of agency services (consumers) be encouraged to participate on these agencies' boards of directors. To assess whether board members would approve of the idea, 183 members were requested to complete a self-administered questionnaire to determine which types of consumers they would prefer to have on the board, & to measure their own attitudes of openness. Hypothesized was that members more open to change would be more accepting of consumers as board members. Although a clear majority of Rs would admit consumers to their boards, the hypothesis was not confirmed. The best predictors of attitudes toward consumers were: (1) knowing a consumer already on the board, (2) evaluation of independence, & (3) being a consumer, as were 10% of the Rs. 2 Tables. D. Abrahams.

____________________________________________________________

Project Equality and Liberal Catholic Reform: Affirmative Action and the National Catholic Conference for Interracial Justice, 1960-1973

Author: O'Reilly, Kenneth11 Marquette U, Milwaukee WI 53233

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61455841?accountid=14667

Abstract: The history of Project Equality is traced from its inception in 1963, as a pilot program of the national Catholic Conference for Interracial Justice, to its present status as a privately backed affirmative action program whose religious orientation is interfaith rather than exclusively Catholic. Its success as a force to encourage minority hiring through refusal to patronize companies that did not follow policies of nondiscrimination & affirmative action is discussed, as is its subsequent decline. Such problems as management inefficiency, difficulties accompanying dependence on foundations & grants, lack of sufficient funds, administrative setbacks, & reluctance on the part of some Catholics to apply structured solutions to social justice situations all contributed to the changes in Project Equality. D. Abrahams.

Factors Associated with Social Action and Convening: A Study of the National Conference of Catholic Charities

Author: Dendinger, Donald11 U Nebraska, Omaha 68101

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61531383?accountid=14667

Abstract: Investigated were factors affecting organizational change in social action & convening programs in 146 affiliated agencies of the National Conference of Catholic Charities (NCCC). Factors included orientations of directors of agencies & internal & external variables which could impact the agency. Data were gathered by means of a mailed questionnaire. Analysis of internal factors revealed that more total income & personnel were positively associated with more extensive social action & convening programs, but a high number of professional personnel was negatively associated. Viewing external factors, high government funding was associated positively with more extensive social action & convening programs, as were higher percentages of non-Catholics & minorities. 7 Tables. Modified AA.

Family Mental Health in a Pluralistic Society

Author: Mostwin, Danuta11 1300 Malvern Ave, Baltimore MD 21204

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61500196?accountid=14667

Abstract: Many Americans belong to subcultural groups, & should be viewed in terms of their subgroup characteristics, specific values, & attitudes. Several US families of Eastern & Central European background were studied to point out the similarities & diversities among these cultural groups; the leading values are subsumed under two rubrics: "The Golden Rule" & "The National Myth." Knowledge of & sensitivity to ethnic diversity can be used to improve family mental health. Part of this knowledge is understanding of the process of ethnic identity formation, which leads to creation of a new form of cultural identity "that is neither with the country of origin nor with the receiving country, but constitutes a third value, the integration of selective cultural patterns specific for the individual & his unique situation." Modified AA.

After Abuse: Child Coping Patterns and Social Work Intervention

Author: Timberlake, Elizabeth M11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20036

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61555017?accountid=14667

Abstract: Hypothesized was that a child victim of physical abuse who has been removed from his family develops a lifestyle of overt aggression & depression. Theoretical perspectives & research methodology were combined to study the social functioning of 56 physically abused children, in the social environments of school & foster home, as associated with patterns of coping with early abuse & deprivation, & with actual parent-child separation & loss. A multiple stepwise regression analysis of the association among overt aggressive behaviors, learned aggressive patterns of coping, depressive process, & social situation obtained a Multiple R of .81, significant at the .05 level. In social situations which stimulated concomitant recognition of aggressive impulse & depressive process, the children resorted to earlier learned patterns of coping with overwhelming feelings. Suggested is a long-range social work goal to break both the compulsively repetitious pattern of aggression & depression within the child's current social situations, & that of aggressive/abusive behavior between parent & child found across generations. 2 Tables. Modified Author Summary.

Psychological Grounds for Church Annulments: Changing Canonical Practice

Author: Green, Thomas J11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61500254?accountid=14667

Abstract: Grounds recently deemed acceptable for annulments granted by church tribunals are reviewed with reference to their psychological components. Historical perspective indicates that previously permissible reasons for annulment -- mental incapacity (insanity) & mental discretion -- were precursors of the new psychological grounds for nullity. The latest decisions emphasize the necessity of being able to undertake & fulfill marital obligations; an incapacity "may be rooted in amentia (insanity), pathological psychic disorders at times affecting the sexual area, or any personality disorder seriously damaging the intellect as well." The following elements are examined in determining marital commitment: (1) a permanent & faithful commitment to marriage partner, (2) receptiveness to children & ability to care for them, (3) stability, (4) emotional maturity, (5) financial responsibility, & (6) ability to cope with ordinary stresses of marriage. Failure to satisfy these measures of commitment constitutes psychological grounds for annulment. D. Abrahams.

Some Theoretical Teaching/Learning Guidelines for the Planning of Family Life Education and Enrichment (Famlee) Programs

Author: Preister, Steven11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20036

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61555256?accountid=14667

Abstract: Various proposals have been made for effective Family Life Education & Enrichment (Famlee) programs. Many of the suggested theoretical frameworks have not been researched; but reference to their guidelines is preferable to random program design. Variables that can differentiate one Famlee program from another include: the particular characteristics of the socializing agent; orientation toward social group differences; consideration of stage of life, tasks, & needs of clients; & locally specified purposes & objectives. An overview of the relevant literature is provided for use in Famlee program design, all of which should encourage personal growth. 1 Figure. D. Abrahams.

Ethnicity in Social Work

Author: Kolm, Richard11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61455795?accountid=14667

Abstract: Within the ever-changing patterns of social interaction, ethnic elements shape the lives of individuals in groups & in society as a whole; they enhance or impede their growth & life chances, condition & channel their behavior, & facilitate or limit their self-realization. Ethnic patterns are significant because of their unique cultural content, derived historically, but based on internalized values. Since ethnicity conditions individual personalities & identities, no interpretation of human personality, & thus no effective approach to human problems, is possible without it. Social work practice, therefore, needs to adopt a more comprehensive theoretical framework which includes the sociocultural elements; this could result in major changes in the conceptualization of human growth & in professional attitudes, knowledge, & skills. S. Karganovic.

Evaluation of Change as a Tool in Treatment

Author: Richter, Phyllis11 National Catholic School Social Service Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61513359?accountid=14667

Abstract: The goal of every treatment is to enable the client to assume responsibility for needed modification (change) in his/her behavior. The initial problem is usually to help the client overcome fear of change. Once that has been accomplished, change made during the treatment period can actually enhance the treatment process; review & evaluation of changes being made become part of the process. In the first interview case worker & client consider what changes are needed; then the changes are effected, & finally evaluated to determine the progress made in the course of treatment. A problem to be faced is that of regression; clients will not be so discouraged by it if the worker explains that it is a normal phenomenon, & that perfection is not to be expected. S. Karganovic.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Evaluation+of+Change+as+a+Tool+in+Treatment&amp;rft.au=Richter%2C+Phyllis&amp;rft.aulast=Richter&amp;rft.aufirst=Phyllis&amp;rft.date=1978-01-01&amp;rft.volume=4&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.spage=15&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Human Rights

Author: Harrington, Patrick J11 National Catholic Secretariat, Monrovia Liberia

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61562897?accountid=14667

Abstract: A program of action to implement human rights should include educating people to understand the dignity of the human person, fostering the idea of service in educational institutions, publicly defending the rights of the poor & oppressed, & ensuring the curtailment of arbitrary arrest & imprisonment. Social organizations should be mobilized in furtherance of human rights. Churches, with unique access to the consciences of many, should stress the social dimension of Christianity. Governments should pursue programs to alleviate poverty & abolish dehumanizing conditions. Foreign companies pursuing business in poor countries should reassess arrogant attitudes & address the questions of just wages & exploitation of raw materials. S. Karganovic.

Humanistic Studies in the Social Work Curriculum

Author: Sokolowski, Robert11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61520063?accountid=14667

Abstract: Challenged are many current assumptions concerning the liberal arts & their place in professional education. Details of their curriculum are discussed, & three areas of study proposed: mastery of language, exposure to history & literature, & a philosophical understanding of basic distinctions, all of which are interrelated. Such an education is not a mere appendage to professional training, but a necessary element if the student is to become a thoughtful & humane person. There is truth to be achieved & conveyed in the humanities, not just opinion or techniques. Professional schools can make an important contribution to the preservation & development of the liberal arts as a human heritage. Modified AA.

Characteristics of Foster Families

Author: Lindholm, Byron W1; Touliatos, John1 Auburn U, AL 38630

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61553296?accountid=14667

Abstract: To determine & analyze similar & dissimilar characteristics, 472 foster families were interviewed in the US & Canada in 1975/76; regional & agency differences in foster family service were examined also. The foster children's current age, sex, ethnicity, health, age at placement, stay in care, & reasons for placement were examined, as were foster parents' age, SC, ethnicity, religion, marriage, children, health, & housing. In addition, the natural parents' age, SC, ethnicity, religion, marriage, & children were studied. Findings for each of the categories are summarized. Results are generally consistent with those of previous research. S. Karganovic.

Friendship, Helping Relations, and Intimacy on Skid Row

Author: Rooney, James F11 Catholic U America, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61512419?accountid=14667

Abstract: The disaffiliation hypothesis proposed by A. Vexilard (no publication information available) was tested: that residence on skid row results in loss of social relationships & of the need for personal contact. A structured questionnaire survey was conducted with 300 randomly selected skid row residents in Philadelphia to investigate the number & location of friends, degree of intimacy with a closest friend, conception of friendship, & help giving. The findings ran counter to Vexilard's postulate. Degree of intimacy to a closest friend has no relationship to the number of friends, but is related to defining friendship as personal commitment. Giving help to friends, by contrast, is positively related both to the number of friends & to defining friendship as utilitarian, but bears no consistent relationship to intimacy. The hypothesis that affiliation is related to alcohol consumption was upheld. Modified AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Friendship%2C+Helping+Relations%2C+and+Intimacy+on+Skid+Row&amp;rft.au=Rooney%2C+James+F&amp;rft.aulast=Rooney&amp;rft.aufirst=James&amp;rft.date=1977-10-01&amp;rft.volume=3&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.spage=31&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Building Community through Faith and Service

Author: Jadot, Archbishop Jean11 3339 Massachusetts Ave NW, Washington DC 20008

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61564698?accountid=14667

Abstract: One cannot sufficiently emphasize the need to build community. Recent years have seen a significant decrease of supportive communities, & the task is to restore & rebuild, to provide a sense of stability, a feeling of personal acceptance, ready assistance in a crisis, & an attachment to a local habitat. Catholic Charities should devote its skill in interpersonal relationships & community organization to this task, but with the objective of a Christian community. Modified AA.

The Concept of Health and the Right to Health Care

Author: Boyle, Joseph M, Jr11 Coll St Thomas, St Paul MN 55105

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61572767?accountid=14667

Abstract: Whether people have a right to health care, or whether being healthy is primarily a matter of individual responsibility, is discussed in terms of the concept of health. Although people do have the responsibility to care for themselves, a community committed to health care has the responsibility to provide its members with medical care on an equal basis. P. Montgomery.

The Health Services System: Dilemmas and Potential Solutions

Author: Schumaker, C J, Jr11 Office Assistant Secretary Defense (Health Affairs) OPPA, Room 1B657 Pentagon Washington DC 20301

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61512455?accountid=14667

Abstract: Competing demands & performance criteria imposed upon the health services system are discussed. Through a review of the literature, conceptual & operational limitations associated with criteria used to assess the performance of the health services system are presented. Contributing to the difficulties in resolving the problems of the health system are two competitive orientations regarding the nature of the problems. One assumes that the source of the problems exists in the dominant institutions of society, & that only by changing them can changes in the health system occur. The opposing view holds that the origins of the problems lie in the life styles of the individual consumers, & only through their alteration can the problems be resolved. Despite this seemingly impossible state of affairs, there is emerging a movement which draws upon both perspectives & is having some successes. The self-care movement, coupled with holistic orientations, is showing promise, in that it involves the consumer & other agents of society in the resolution of problems. It has been applied in poor & nonpoor sectors of society with apparently similar results. AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=The+Health+Services+System%3A+Dilemmas+and+Potential+Solutions&amp;rft.au=Schumaker%2C+C+J%2C+Jr&amp;rft.aulast=Schumaker&amp;rft.aufirst=C&amp;rft.date=1977-07-01&amp;rft.volume=3&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=19&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=The+Health+Services+System%3A+Dilemmas+and+Potential+Solutions&amp;rft.au=Schumaker%2C+C+J%2C+Jr&amp;rft.aulast=Schumaker&amp;rft.aufirst=C&amp;rft.date=1977-07-01&amp;rft.volume=3&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.spage=19&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

America's Low-Income Housing Efforts: The Poor as Hostages of Fear and Misperception

Author: Lawlor, John J

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61534487?accountid=14667

Abstract: Misconceptions about the National Housing Acts that have resulted in lack of support for public housing are discussed. Among the myths are: (1) the belief that public housing means low-income, highrise apartment complexes; (2) the belief that only the poor benefit from federal housing legislation; & (3) the fear that federal housing projects lead to resegregation of neighborhoods.
