Social Work in Industry: A History and a Viewpoint

Author: Carter, Irl11 School Social Work U Iowa, Iowa City 52242

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61496143?accountid=14667

Abstract: The development of social work & welfare programs in US industry is examined. Industrial social work, mainly philanthropic in the mid-1800s, was expanded during WWI to include areas such as physical, cultural, economic, & personal welfare. Following the 1920s, it declined during the Depression, but was reestablished with federal funding during WWII. The role of schools of social work in this field is discussed, & the future of social work in industry is examined. P. Montgomery.

Social Policy and the Right to Work

Author: Gil, David G11 Brandeis U, Waltham MA 02154

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61572659?accountid=14667

Abstract: Based on an examination of the concepts "social policies," "societal values relevant to social policies," "rights," & "work," several questions related to "the right to work" are explored. The right to work is differentiated from the right to a job; the latter constitutes a possible reform within the prevailing economic-political system, but the former requires a radical transformation of the system to guarantee all humans access to & use of sufficient productive resources to sustain existence & enhance the quality of life. The myths of self-reliance & the work ethic are critically analyzed. Modified AA.

Social Treatment: An Emerging Concept

Author: Summers, Mace11 Fauquier Family Guidance Center, Warrenton VA 22186

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61533780?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of the history & characteristics of social treatment as a method for counteracting emotional disturbances. Social functioning is an individual's ability to successfully fulfill multiple roles. Social treatment, which involves the development of social competence through interventions emphasizing a range of experiences, has five major features: (1) The focus is on external behavior rather than internal psychological phenomena. (2) Social functioning & coping are the standards used for setting goals & measuring progress. (3) The model is one of growth, developing social skills, rather than an illness- or deficit- functioning model. (4) The basic orientation is social learning theory. (5) Educational modalities of intervention are a major part of therapy. J. Schulman.

Contracting as an Element in Therapy

Author: Kempf, Sharon

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61434496?accountid=14667

Abstract: An overview of the therapeutic process of contracting. A reciprocal process between social worker & client, the therapeutic contract is based on four elements: (1) what each participant expects to achieve from the exchange; (2) reasons for coming together; (3) what each expects to do; & (4) rights & responsibilities of each. The purposes of therapeutic contracting are identified, as are underlying assumptions. J. Schulman.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Contracting+as+an+Element+in+Therapy&amp;rft.au=Kempf%2C+Sharon&amp;rft.aulast=Kempf&amp;rft.aufirst=Sharon&amp;rft.date=1976-10-01&amp;rft.volume=2&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.spage=27&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

Strategies for Developing Citizen Participation in Low Socio-Economic Areas

Author: Brabson, Howard V11 U Michigan, Ann Arbor 48104

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61567331?accountid=14667

Abstract: Examined are modes & areas of participation by members of low SE groups in community activities related to their welfare. The frame of reference is community organization as a social work method, using a community development model, & the basis is a recent study of citizen participation in a low SE area in a midwestern US U town. Statistical analysis of 263 interview responses produced these findings: (1) high % of involvement in community activities; (2) low % of participation in the policy-making mode; (3) significant r between locus of control & involvement in all areas of participation; & (4) high r between participation in task-oriented committees & voluntary contributions & locus of control. Since decisions affecting economic & social development are made in the political arena, the community organization practitioner should work toward increasing participation in political organizations & policy making. 4 Tables. Modified AA.

Links: http://mgetit.lib.umich.edu/?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;ctx_enc=info:ofi/enc:UTF-8&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/ProQ%3Asocialservicesshell&amp;rft_val_fmt=info:ofi/fmt:kev:mtx:journal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Social+Thought&amp;rft.atitle=Strategies+for+Developing+Citizen+Participation+in+Low+Socio-Economic+Areas&amp;rft.au=Brabson%2C+Howard+V&amp;rft.aulast=Brabson&amp;rft.aufirst=Howard&amp;rft.date=1976-10-01&amp;rft.volume=2&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.spage=41&amp;rft.isbn=&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rft.title=Social+Thought&amp;rft.issn=0099183X&amp;rft_id=info:doi/

A Study of Regional Variation in Adoption Placement Patterns

Author: Touliatos, John1; Lindholm, Byron W1 Auburn U, AL 38630

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61456557?accountid=14667

Abstract: Presented are data confirming two hypotheses regarding the placement of children for adoption: (1) Demographic variables of placement differ from region to region. (2) Frequency of finding homes for hard-to-place children is related to flexibility in placement practices & proper use of regional resources. Data were obtained in 1974 from 67 agencies serving 530 adoptive families in the US & Canada. 4 Tables. Modified Author Conclusion.

Renewal at Mid-Decade: An Effort by an Agency

Author: McGeady, Sister Mary Rose11 Catholic Charities Diocese Brooklyn, NY 11202

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61533875?accountid=14667

Abstract: A presentation of how the Brooklyn Catholic Charities (BCC) applied the directives of the National Conference of Catholic Charities (five value-oriented & five service-oriented statements) to better service a population of two and a half million Catholics, including a heavy representation of financially struggling immigrants. The BCC devised a three-part restructuring program: (1) creating a regional director's position for each of the 5 vicariates in the diocese, (2) opening local human service centers in all vicariates, & (3) putting services for the aged, handicapped, & needy, as well as family services, in each local community. Obstacles impeding optimal operation included image problems, value conflicts, time vs task problems, ambiguities of task assignments, & delivery system problems. J. Schulman.

Genetics and Responsible Parenthood

Author: Haring, Bernard

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61512611?accountid=14667

Abstract: The need for parental responsibility in producing a healthy gene pool for the future is discussed. To achieve this eugenic goal, parents need to be informed about: (1) genetic risks involved with mate selection, (2) X-linked genetic disorders & faulty genes, & (3) possible effect of timing of intercourse on the health of offspring. Nonmanipulative genetic counselors should be made available to all sectors of the population. The moral difference between voluntary & involuntary sterilization is also discussed. J. Schulman.

The Making of a Person: A Psycho-Social Analysis

Author: Bardill, Donald R11 School Social Work Catholic U, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61515841?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of the relational approach to human behavior as a method of understanding important relationships among different life systems. Analysis is based on the interrelationships of four life-realities; self, other, context, & spirituality. Interactions between these realities are operationalized in specific life stances. Clinical social work involves understanding the developmental factors & behavioral consequences of these stances. Modified Author Summary.

Individualism and Communalism: Two or One?

Author: Falck, Hans S11 Menninger Foundation, Topeka KS 66601

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61456358?accountid=14667

Abstract: A comparison of individualism & communalism as methods of directing interpersonal behavior. Whereas individualism is thought to result in a dysfunctional set of rules governing behavior, communalism is believed to instill a personal sense of manageability of one's environment. Definitions for individualism, individuation, & communalism are formulated, & the consequences of each approach outlined. J. Schulman.

Symbolic Consciousness: A Synthetic Approach to Moral Development

Author: Thompson, Andrew11 Catholic U, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61522756?accountid=14667

Abstract: Development of a symbolic consciousness can promote moral growth in children. The symbolic model can also be used to identify stages of moral development. In using this approach, social workers & educators should understand that the cognitive & social realms cannot be spearated without decreasing effectiveness. Although the model is not ready for general application, several guidelines for its use are suggested: (1) Social workers & educators must first develop their own symbolic consciousness. (2) They must also become more sensitive to relevant aspects of a youth's moral development or problems. (3) Then they can assist the youth in developing his/her own symbolic consciousness. Modified Author Conclusion.

Public Social Policy and the Developmental Years

Author: Judah, Eleanor Hannon11 School Social Work Catholic U, Washington DC 20017

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61565008?accountid=14667

Abstract: The need for children to be protected by a public social policy is discussed. Emphasized is family breakdown & its consequences for children in their developmental years. Most current social service provisions for families & children fall under three guidelines of Title XX of the Social Security Act: (1) achieving & maintaining economic self-support to prevent, reduce, or eliminate poverty; (2) achieving or maintaining self-sufficiency, & (3) preventing or remedying neglect, abuse, or exploitation of children & adults not able to protect their own interests. The bases for social policy -- eg, values, norms, beliefs, science, & technology -- are discussed, & data on families & children are presented. J. Schulman.

Evolution from Custodial Care to Residential Treatment

Author: Vitillo, Robert11 Catholic Family & Community Services, Paterson NJ 07509

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61520019?accountid=14667

Abstract: A discussion of the evolution of Mount Saint Joseph Children's Center, Totona, NJ, from a custodial care home to a residential treatment center. Six policy considerations are examined: (1) validity of institutional care, (2) residential treatment of emotionally disturbed & socially maladjusted children, (3) administrative management, (4) model of service delivery, (5) educational arrangements, & (6) program assessment. Valid alternatives for a comprehensive child care system include foster families, group homes, & institutional care. The capabilities & needs of each child must be considered to determine the best alternative. J. Schulman.

Use of 'Significant Other' in Group Process for Adolescents

Author: Pazzaglini, Gino1; Hanson, Margaret1 Catholic Social Services Broome County, Binghamton NY 13902

http://proxy.lib.umich.edu/login?url=http://search.proquest.com/docview/61565314?accountid=14667

Abstract: Discussed is the need for direct service agencies to provide opportunities for creating "significant other" relationships for children without a suitable adult model. An adult-child relationship within a group work approach is recommended. A case example is provided from the Catholic Social Services of Broome County, NY. J. Schulman.
